Four-Nation Naval Agreement Expected to be Signed This Week. Britain Does Not Insist on Seeking Germany's Consent. France Abandons the Issue of Linking Naval and Air Force Armaments.

London. Naval circles believe that the qualitative limitation agreement for naval forces can be formally signed within this week. Britain originally intended to seek Germany's consent before signing the four-nation naval agreement, but has now abandoned this proposal. The draft agreement does not include political issues or issues related to the mutual connection between naval and air force armaments. (Havas dispatch on the 25th)

London. After the British delegation to the Naval Conference held talks with the delegations of the countries concerned, including the US delegation, last week, it has now become clear that political issues should not be mixed into the technical agreement on qualitative limitations of naval forces. Otherwise, the final failure is inevitable. The Italian delegation has expressed its views on the fact that the country was unable to participate in the political agreement during the sanctions period. The French delegation requested that the issue of air force armament limitation be resolved before inviting Germany to participate in the naval agreement. The US delegation was limited by the instructions of its own government and had no right to sign any protocol or agreement containing political clauses. Seeing that the attitudes of these countries were mutually contradictory, Britain changed its attitude and considered the establishment of a technical agreement to be sufficient. In addition, the British government had contacted the German government through diplomatic channels last night in order to obtain information on Germany's shipbuilding program based on the Anglo-German Naval Agreement in May last year, so that it was not necessary to invite Germany to participate in the naval agreement. (Havas News Agency dispatch on the 25th)

London. Chief Representative Picia of the Naval Conference and British Naval Minister Monsell held a long meeting today. Picia informed Monsell of Rome's latest instructions. The meeting lasted from 3:30 pm to 6:30 pm. Both men were silent after the meeting, but it is not admitted that Picia raised the issue of sanctions. It is generally speculated that Italy will reiterate that the Italian government's signature on naval treaties is conditional on the satisfactory resolution of political disputes. US Chief Representative Davis then visited Monsell. The situation at the Naval Conference has not seen any progress today. Monsell will meet with Picia again tomorrow. France is now also firmly insisting that any naval treaties involve political events, while Davis is strongly opposed to this action, so the Naval Conference is now clearly in a very difficult position. (Reuters dispatch on the 24th)

London. Italy notified Britain today that Italy has no intention of signing the naval agreement until the League of Nations cancels the sanctions plan and the British Navy withdraws its increased fleet from the Mediterranean. This move is tantamount to a blow to the London Naval Conference. US Chief Representative Davis and British Naval Minister Monsell held a two-hour meeting to discuss the recent developments. Davis expressed surprise today at the statement made by the French representative that France is now awaiting Washington's reply to Paris's proposal to limit the tonnage and caliber of battleships, saying that he had notified the French representative of the United States' unwillingness to express its approval of this limitation. (National Telegram on the 24th)

Inventor of Airplane Bombs Invents Super Dreadnought; U.S. Navy Department Considering His Plan

Stanford, USA – Mr. Barr, the inventor of airplane bombs, today claimed that he has invented a super dreadnought that is invulnerable to torpedo attacks, heavy artillery bombardment, and aerial explosions. This battleship has an outer protective armor made of non-metallic materials. The ship is equipped with two torpedo launchers on each side, capable of firing torpedoes two at a time per minute. Each ship has a tonnage of at least 85,000 tons and a speed of 15 nautical miles per hour. According to Mr. Barr, the U.S. Navy Department is currently considering his plan, and both the Soviet Union and the United Kingdom also want to purchase his plan. (National Telegram, 24th)

British Foreign Secretary Addresses the House of Commons on the International Situation; Strengthen Military Affairs and Uphold Collective Security; Opposition Party Advocates Immediate Oil Embargo

London – After assuming the position of British Foreign Secretary, Mr. Eden made his first important statement in the House of Commons last night regarding the international situation. His speech can be divided into three parts: the first part concerned the Abyssinian (Ethiopian) question, the second part presented his views on some events not directly related to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, and the third part discussed the general international situation, explaining the reasons why Britain must increase military expenditure. The British Foreign Secretary's speech was made during a debate on foreign affairs in the House of Commons.

Opposition leader Mr. Smith initiated the debate, criticizing the government's indecision on the sanctions issue. He advocated that the government should strive to implement an oil embargo immediately and stop supplying aggressor nations with livestock, cotton, and other goods. Liberal Party leader Mr. Sinclair agreed with the above proposal, saying that even if the United States does not participate in the oil embargo, it must be implemented, and coal, iron, copper, and other materials should also be embargoed to completely sever economic relations with Italy. Conservative Mr. Amery uniquely held a dissenting view, advising the government not to blindly follow sanctions, but to seek solutions based on the advantages and disadvantages of the matter, rather than on the idea of punishing Italy.

Achievements of Sanctions Against Italy

Foreign Secretary Mr. Eden rose to speak amidst applause, recounting past events, saying that within ten days after the outbreak of the war, Italy was declared an aggressor nation by the League of Nations' Executive Council, and this verdict was subsequently approved by fifty member states in the General Assembly. A committee was then established to propose four measures for implementing sanctions against Italy. The noteworthy achievement was the speed of progress, rather than delay. The tasks undertaken by the Coordination Committee and its subcommittees were the arduous work of planning sanctions. The sanctions on financial matters and the rejection of Italian exports could not, of course, be immediately effective; this was obviously visible. The goal was to gradually replace Italy's purchasing power with that of other countries.

Italy's Financial Resources Are Gradually Depleted

According to statistics, Italy's exports to League of Nations member states usually account for 70% of its total exports. Now, the aggressor nation's purchasing power abroad has been greatly reduced as a result of the sanctions. A country in this situation can, of course, continue to purchase abroad to the extent permitted by its gold reserves and foreign exchange, but in this situation, the country's funds will inevitably decrease rapidly, and eventually it will completely lose its purchasing power. Looking at Italy's recent efforts, it can be seen that Italy is now deeply aware of the importance of sanctions. The impact of the war is continuous and cumulative, and will eventually have an important force to achieve the main goal of the League of Nations. What is the main goal? That is, a ceasefire.

Study of the Oil Embargo Issue

What the League of Nations is currently considering is the sanctions on goods, and the source of supply of these goods is mostly in the hands of non-League of Nations member states. In their view, the oil embargo is the same as the sanctions on other goods, and must be judged by the same standard, that is, whether its implementation can help to stop the war. Because stopping the war is the common goal of all countries attending the Geneva Conference, governments must study it in this spirit and then decide. As for how to decide, he cannot say anything, because the governments of the League of Nations member states are currently carefully studying the expert report, which has not yet been completed.

Britain Still Acts Collectively

The British government has done what it can to facilitate the convening of this committee. The sooner the committee can decide, the more beneficial it will be to the matter. At the same time, the British government has not abandoned its original resolution on the oil embargo in principle, nor has it canceled its determination to take collective action with other League of Nations member states on agreed matters. The British government's policy remains to maintain a steady and collective resistance to aggression. Any decision of the British government should be based on the spirit of the League of Nations itself. There should be no sign of weakness or concession until a peace agreement is signed.

The League of Nations' Credibility Has Greatly Increased

We should not weaken our support for the League of Nations simply because it is not omnipotent. Although the League of Nations cannot accomplish everything, it has never failed to accomplish many things. In the past eighteen months, the League of Nations' credibility has greatly increased, and its power has come with its credibility. Today, some people regard the League of Nations as a dangerous object, but anyone who knows a little about diplomacy does not regard the League of Nations as insignificant today. The League of Nations has two qualities: one is the passive task of the police, and the other is the constructive work of mediators and peacemakers. The two are completely different. What people urgently hope for is to see a satisfactory solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute.

Peace Negotiations Have Not Been Abandoned

At this point in his speech, the British Foreign Secretary proceeded to describe the report of the Five-Nation Committee appointed by the League of Nations' Executive Council last September to study the basis for a solution that would satisfy all parties, saying that unfortunately, the terms of the report were not accepted by the Italian government at the time. However, from the British government's point of view, this report can still serve as the basis for future mediation. He felt that it was necessary to explain what kind of purpose the League of Nations held when conducting sanctions. Although sanctions are unwelcome to all of us, they are tools to achieve our goals, and the goal is to establish a solution in accordance with the principles of the League of Nations, so that both sides have a lasting and normal relationship. He hoped that the Five-Nation Committee's report would not be forgotten or shelved. According to the British government, the appropriate place to reopen peace talks is Geneva, because the atmosphere there is the most suitable.

When he goes to Geneva again to discuss the sanctions issue in the future, he will make clear and precise statements with the full agreement of the House of Commons, declaring that the British government and people are willing to actively cooperate with other countries to implement sanctions, but are willing to see peace restored between Italy and Abyssinia on a fair basis first.

The Covenant Does Not Need to be Revised

The Foreign Secretary finally mentioned the proposal to amend the League of Nations Covenant, saying that now is not the appropriate time to revise the Covenant. He then touched on the issue of raw materials, saying that the government is willing to study the issue of colonial raw materials mentioned by Sir Samuel Hoare at any time, but this is ultimately not a panacea. This issue is extremely complex.

Two Conditions for a Collective System

The Foreign Secretary then generally discussed the international situation, saying that eighteen years after the Great War, countries are again encountering terrible problems that are exactly the same as those encountered before 1914, which makes the collective intelligence of the world lose its effectiveness. The most urgent task for politicians today is to find an effective intelligence to prevent war from happening again. If Britain wants to participate in collective security, then two conditions are essential:

The security system should be truly collective and powerful, sufficient to deter the ambition of any aggressor.

Britain's policy and military force to fulfill its full responsibility in this system should be fully powerful and determined.

The Foreign Secretary continued, "We must clearly distinguish this policy from a policy of encirclement when we reiterate our support for the League of Nations and the collective security system. What the British government wants is to fulfill its responsibilities in the collective security system, not to participate in encirclement operations. Military expenditure must now be greatly increased. This is something to regret, but there is comfort in this plan, because reorganizing military preparations to consolidate the collective security system is the cheapest way to reorganize military preparations."

Reasons for Strengthening Military Preparations

The Foreign Secretary concluded by saying that now, because of the lack of trust in the goodwill of various countries, and because terror is coming from all sides, we really have to reorganize our military preparations. Gradually strengthening the collective security system is the only way to eliminate the terror of unwarranted aggression. It must wait until all countries know that, no matter what, aggression does not pay off, and then it will be over. Labor Party leader Mr. Attlee expressed great disappointment with the Foreign Secretary's speech, saying that the government's indecision on the League of Nations issue cannot give the country a unified direction. The case of Britain's increase in military preparations will be brought up, and the required military preparations are only for the League of Nations. The Labor Party is unwilling to support the increase in military preparations, and the policies of imperialism and alliance.

Italy's Trade Decreases Sharply

Mr. Cranborne finally concluded the debate, saying that sanctions are now gradually taking effect, and Italy's export trade has been greatly hit. Britain's actions in the Mediterranean are purely defensive. Since Britain has taken on collective security, Britain's words and deeds are consistent, which is the greatest guarantee on which peace can rely. He continued, saying that the whole world is now feeling uneasy, and Britain is the mainstay. We should make this mainstay strong and stable. The reason for Britain's reconsideration of military preparations lies in this. (Reuters, 25th)

Eden's Speech Disappoints Various Parties Because It Is Vague

London – British Foreign Secretary Mr. Eden's speech in the House of Commons last night disappointed the newspapers of the Labor Party and the Liberal Party, criticizing his remarks as vague. The Conservative Party also believed that Mr. Eden's remarks had no novelty, but approved of his firm statement that Britain abides by the collective security system, and his common sense in dealing with the sanctions issue. The Times said that Mr. Eden's remarks had the full agreement of the cabinet, and that the main point was nothing more than that Britain must re-establish military preparations in order to promote disarmament. If the oil embargo asks for help from the United States, it will provoke the resentment of the majority of the American people, and regard it as the League of Nations wanting to add responsibilities that it does not want to the United States. The Daily Mail and the Daily Express still hold an attitude of opposition to the collective security system, but the Morning Post said that Mr. Eden's remarks did not indicate that the British government wanted to take the lead in imposing new sanctions on Italy. This is gratifying. (Reuters, 25th)

London – When the House of Commons discussed the government's current foreign policy yesterday, Foreign Secretary Eden gave a long speech. Parliamentarians are now commenting on it, believing that the most noteworthy point is the proposal made regarding the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, that is, firmly advocating continuing negotiations and mediation to find a satisfactory solution. As for the general impression, it is that the uneasiness felt by the members of the House of Commons regarding the current situation in Europe has not been removed, and the government's position has not been seen to have strengthened. (Havas, 25th)

League of Nations Personnel are Gratified that the Collective Security System Depends on Britain's Attitude

Geneva – After British Foreign Secretary Mr. Eden gave a speech in the British House of Commons yesterday, League of Nations personnel have been commenting on it, believing that Mr. Eden has expressed opposition to the proposal to revise the League of Nations Covenant, and therefore a certain country's proposal to revise the Covenant must be postponed for discussion. They also believe that Foreign Secretary Eden's speech was not very clear on the Abyssinian issue, and the reason for this is that the 18-nation subcommittee of the League of Nations General Assembly is about to meet, and it is appropriate to be cautious in handling matters. As for the entire speech, it still expresses approval of the collective security system. This is particularly gratifying. In short, the collective security organization that European countries can complete according to the various principles of the League of Nations Covenant can be successful. The main factor depends on Britain's attitude towards the League of Nations. In addition, the attitude that Britain should take when the 18-nation subcommittee meets can also be seen from the principles mentioned by Foreign Secretary Eden in his speech. (Havas, 25th)

Geneva – After the League of Nations members read British Foreign Secretary Mr. Eden's speech in the House of Commons, they all believed that Britain's concern for Germany's rearmament far exceeded its concern for the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. This was also the focus of the previous Hoare-Laval plan, which was to shift Italy's intentions and rebuild the Stresa Front against Germany. Mr. Eden's resolution to give a speech today can be said to be a rehash of old matters. Although this is quite alarming to the League of Nations representatives here, Mr. Eden still emphasized the point of collective peace, which has been able to dispel the concerns of people here that Britain is about to strike the League of Nations' policy towards Italy. (National Telegram, 24th)

Paris is Deeply Impressed, Believing that it Does Not Conflict with French Policy

Paris – British Foreign Secretary Mr. Eden's speech in the House of Commons, firmly declaring that Britain's sanctions policy against Italy will continue unchanged, has aroused a deep impression in all circles in Paris. Everyone believes that the policy taken by the British government does not conflict with the attitude taken by the French government. The attitude of the French government is that France will give full support to any collective action passed by the League of Nations' Executive Council, but France will not initiate anything in this matter. Mr. Eden's statement that Britain now needs to reorganize its military preparations for the sake of collective security is also sincerely welcomed by all parties in France. (Reuters, 25th)

Italian Authorities Observe that Tightening Sanctions is Enough to Increase Britain's Responsibility

Rome – After British Foreign Secretary Mr. Eden's speech in the British House of Commons yesterday was transmitted here, responsible parties declared that, based on Foreign Secretary Eden's speech, it can be known that if the move to tighten sanctions against Italy is indeed implemented, then the responsibility borne by Britain will be increased. Britain has already seen this. (Havas, 25th)

British House of Commons Passes Additional Military Expenditure; Navy Department Proposes Ship-Building Plan

London – The House of Commons held a closed-door meeting today to discuss national defense issues. The Navy Department will propose a naval shipbuilding plan. The cabinet, because France, Italy, Japan, and the United States are competing to add destroyers, has recently decided to add nine such warships, each of 1,350 tons. In the House of Commons, some people strongly advocate building seven more destroyers of 1,850 tons. Birmingham – Former British Foreign Secretary Mr. Austen Chamberlain gave a speech here today, saying that there is absolutely no reason to be surprised by the United States' expansion of military preparations, and Britain will never go to war with the United States, but since the eagerness to prepare for war has spread throughout Europe, and even Switzerland and the Netherlands are caught up in the whirlpool, and the suspicion and apprehension of all parties are so great, then Britain should not lag behind alone. (National Telegram, 24th)

Franco-Russian Treaty; French Congress Still Discussing; Foreign Minister Declares to Explain to the Cabinet

Paris – According to what this agency's parliamentary correspondent knows, regarding the Franco-Russian mutual assistance agreement, the Chamber of Deputies will not be able to complete discussions before Thursday. Many deputies are still scheduled to speak and express their opinions. (Havas, 25th)

Paris – The Chamber of Deputies is scheduled to vote on the ratification of the Franco-Russian mutual assistance treaty tomorrow. Foreign Minister Mr. Flandin will personally attend and give a speech. This afternoon, the cabinet held a meeting, and Mr. Flandin will explain the main points of the speech he intends to read tomorrow. After the cabinet meeting, Mr. Flandin met with Soviet Ambassador Mr. Potemkin. (Havas, 24th)

Moscow – The Zhenli Bao's Paris correspondent held talks with Mr. Penko, the Minister of the French League of Nations. Mr. Penko described the Franco-Soviet pact, saying, "The great line I initiated is now being realized. The parliament will ratify this pact, which is already self-evident. The great significance of this pact for France and the peace line has been said by Mr. Doumergue tomorrow. The Franco-Soviet pact is a weapon to consolidate peace, and therefore can strengthen the League of Nations and consolidate the relationship between countries that desire peace. This pact includes the huge political power of the Soviet collective security system. France and the Soviet Union are the two geographical poles of the European continent, and now they have strengthened their friendship to consolidate peace policy." (Tass, 25th)

Italy and Abyssinia Peace Treaty; Someone Proposes New Plan; Based on League of Nations Covenant and Treaty; Relevant Authorities are Studying

London – Regarding the issue of peace between Italy and Abyssinia, a new plan has recently been proposed, and relevant countries are studying it. The general public believes that Italy is extremely willing to consider this plan. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has also sent personnel to Abyssinia in a private capacity to begin contact with the Abyssinian Emperor, so that if the negotiations fail, Italy can still acknowledge it. According to the main principles of this new plan, the 1906 treaty between Britain, France, and Italy on Abyssinia and the obligations stipulated in the League of Nations Covenant are to be integrated in order to satisfy the wishes of all parties. The main points are as follows:

The Italian-Abyssinian dispute should be resolved within the scope of the League of Nations. Some parts of Abyssinian territory may be ceded to Italy, and Italy should pay compensation. Abyssinian mineral resources may be exploited using foreign capital and technology, and part of the surplus profits should be allocated to Abyssinia. All of the Amharic region, that is, the main part of Abyssinia, its sovereignty is still owned by the Abyssinian Emperor.

Regarding the second point, the land that Italy can obtain is: A. the northern regions of Biru and Drou (the land previously conquered by Abyssinia, bordering Italian Eritrea); B. the southern provinces of Wogaidan, Bolan, and Sidamo, bordering British Somaliland or British Kenya. However, Italy should compensate Abyssinia with money. This new plan also advocates that Abyssinia cede the eastern Wossa region, that is, the land through which the Djibouti-Abyssinia Railway passes, to France, and cede the Kunlin-British-Ethiopian Sultanate to Britain. Britain and France should also compensate Abyssinia with money. Finally, it is also advocated that the Abyssinian government should issue a public debt under the management of the League of Nations, and the fund should be filled with mineral surpluses, and the League of Nations should keep it in custody on behalf of the government. (Havas, 24th)

Brussels – A semi-official Belgian communications agency correspondent in London recently declared that, according to well-informed sources, the special envoy sent by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and personnel from the Italian Embassy in Britain are currently attempting to begin negotiations with the British government in order to seek a solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute based on the principles published by British General Corwin in various newspapers. General Corwin's principles include six items: The administrative power of the non-Amharic region of Abyssinia should be ceded to Britain, Italy, and France, and each country should compensate them with money. This money should be handed over to the League of Nations for issuing Abyssinia's public debt to pay interest. This public debt should be used to develop Abyssinia's economy. Most of the non-Amharic region should be ceded to Italy. Its area is equal to the "colonial zone" that British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister Laval advocated that Abyssinia should be划归 to Italy when they proposed a peace plan last December, so as to match the Italian territory's boundary line. The non-Amharic region and the British and French territories should be connected, and should be ceded to Britain and France. Abyssinia's sovereignty and its security should be guaranteed by the League of Nations. After the mineral products in the non-Amharic region are exploited by other countries, a portion of the surplus profits should be allocated to Abyssinia. (Havas Agency, 25th)

League of Nations 18-Nation Committee to Convene on the Second of Next Month to Discuss Tightening Sanctions Against Italy; Frequent Diplomatic Contacts between France and Italy

Rome – The League of Nations General Assembly's 18-Nation Subcommittee is scheduled to meet on the second of next month to discuss the issue of tightening sanctions against Italy. It is rumored that the Italian government will issue an order on that day for warships across the country to fire up their engines in preparation for deployment. This news has recently been acknowledged by officials. (Havas Agency, 24th)

Paris – Foreign Minister Flandin recently met with Italian Ambassador Cerutti. The general public believes that this move must be related to the issue of banning coal and oil. They also believe that when the League of Nations' General Assembly's 18-Nation Subcommittee discusses this issue on the second of next month, the French government will definitely take a passive attitude, that is, the French government is unwilling to evade the measures that the committee can decide, but it is also unwilling to initiate any actions that would make the international situation increasingly tense. On the semi-official side, it is also said that since France is neither a crude oil producing country nor a large-scale sales country, the influence it can have on this issue is naturally limited. (Havas, 24th)

Rome – After Prime Minister Mussolini held talks with German Ambassador Hassel and Polish Ambassador Vesaki, French Foreign Minister Flandin immediately met with Italian Ambassador to France Cerutti. French Ambassador to Italy Chamberlin also contacted Italian Foreign Minister Mr. Suvich. Political figures here have been commenting on it, believing that if the League of Nations' General Assembly's 18-Nation Subcommittee decides to tighten sanctions against Italy when it meets on the second of next month, then there is a possibility that Italy and Germany will cooperate in practice. Although Italy has no intention of abandoning the Locarno Pact, the Stresa Front, and the Franco-Italian Rome Agreement at present, if the League of Nations tightens sanctions, Italy may change its current policy and take Germany's position on major international issues. Political figures here believe that although France's attitude towards Italy can still be said to be returning to good, at present there is still no hope that Britain's policy towards Italy will change. In addition, after the recent successive victories of the expeditionary force led by General Badoglio on the northern road of Abyssinia, people here believe that the Abyssinian army will eventually have a major defeat, and Abyssinian territory will definitely be dismembered. Therefore, British Foreign Secretary Eden's speech in the British House of Commons yesterday, which advocated seeking a solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute based on the recommendations made by the League of Nations' Executive Council's Five-Nation Special Committee in September of last year, has no room for acceptance in Italy. (Havas, 25th)

Rome – Foreign Minister Mr. Suvich received French Ambassador to Italy Chamberlin this afternoon. It is heard that what the two discussed was related to the League of Nations' General Assembly's 18-Nation Subcommittee meeting on March 2nd to discuss tightening sanctions against Italy. (Havas, 24th)

Naval Mutual Assistance Issue: Italy Protests to Britain Again, Maintaining Original Position

Rome: Regarding the issue of naval mutual assistance among Mediterranean coastal nations, Italy previously lodged a protest with Britain, which was rejected. Italian Ambassador to Britain, Grandi, submitted a note to the British Foreign Office this morning, stating that the Italian government maintains its original position on this matter and that "the Italian government reserves the right to re-discuss this issue at an appropriate time." (Havas dispatch, 25th)

London: According to reliable sources in political circles, the British government, as the tense situation in the Mediterranean has passed, will gradually withdraw its fleets stationed there. The aircraft carrier "Courageous" and battleship "Renown" have already been recalled from the Mediterranean to Britain for docking and repairs, which are expected to take several months. This indicates that the British cabinet believes that naval conflicts are unlikely to occur in the Mediterranean. As for the Red Sea, most of the warships originally stationed there from the Far East Fleet, namely four cruisers and all submarines, have also been recalled to Hong Kong. Furthermore, two of the four submarines originally stationed in Aden have been transferred to Port Said in Egypt, and the remaining two have been dispatched to Bombay. This clearly shows that the British cabinet has abandoned its plan to blockade the Red Sea. However, officials are currently keeping these facts secret, fearing that public opinion, seeing the situation in the Mediterranean has eased, would no longer enthusiastically support the government's rearmament plan. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

Military Conference Held at Palazzo Venezia in Italy; Crown Prince Umberto Also Present

Rome: At 4 PM today, Prime Minister Mussolini convened a military conference at Palazzo Venezia. Crown Prince Umberto was also in attendance. (Ginwas dispatch, 24th)

Athens: Although the atmosphere in the Mediterranean has eased slightly, Italy's defense work on the islands of the Dodecanese is becoming increasingly tense. According to reports from here, the strategically important island of Leros has a garrison of 18,000 troops. The island has no contact with the outside world, and the island's residents have been relocated to Rhodes or sent back to Italy. There are six destroyers and ten other major warships anchored in the port, all under the command of Admiral Barcelli. On the island of Corfu, all armaments and heavy artillery, except those defending Mount Ilias, have been transferred to Leros. (Guomin dispatch, 24th)

Difficulties in Italian-German Rapprochement; Hitler and Mussolini Have Divergent Views

Paris: A correspondent for Le Matin in Rome recently stated that after repeated talks between Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and German Ambassador Hassell, both sides believe that active cooperation between Italy and Germany under the current circumstances is not opportune. German Führer Hitler raised several questions regarding Italy's current commercial and military policies, instructing Hassell to inquire about Mussolini's views. Mussolini's answers were not concrete, as Italy's commerce and military have been in a special situation since conducting the war against Abyssinia and resisting international sanctions. Regarding the issue of the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact, Mussolini and Hassell reached a consensus, but both sides failed to agree on whether the obligations stipulated in the Locarno Treaties could be altered due to this agreement. It is generally believed that Mussolini and Hassell will continue consultations in the near future, but the date has not yet been announced. In short, after the recent talks between Italy and Germany, although a better understanding has been achieved, no practical progress has been made. What is known is that the Italian government is currently most concerned with promoting closer ties between Italy and Germany. (Ginwas dispatch, 25th)

George Bernard Shaw Says: The United States Should Befriend Soviet Russia to Prevent Japanese Threat

Honolulu: George Bernard Shaw was welcomed by locals here today. Shaw stated that the United States should firmly maintain its friendly relations with Soviet Russia to prevent the threat from Japan, but also said that there will be no war in the near future because "we are too cowardly." (Guomin dispatch, 24th)

Soviet Union Celebrates Red Army Anniversary; Far East Commander Encourages Troops to Defend Against Aggression and Defend National Territory

Khabarovsk: General Blucher, Commander of the Far East Red Army, issued an order to the Special Far East Red Army on the 18th anniversary of the Red Army, stating, "The Red Army is a powerful force guarding the Soviet border, protecting the happy and prosperous lives of workers and peasants. The Soviet government firmly implements a policy of peace, but the world's imperialist fascist aggressors from both East and West continue to wield their sharp knives against our homeland of the world's workers. In 1929, China's White generals, instigated by world imperialists, attempted to test the Soviet Union's power, but were ultimately defeated. However, this still has not satisfied the enemy. Today, the crisis of military attacks on the Far Eastern border is becoming increasingly urgent. The Far East Red Army must be prepared at all times." (Tass dispatch, 25th)

Japanese Cabinet Decides to Convene Special Diet Session; Meeting to Open on March 20th for Three Weeks

Tokyo: This morning's cabinet meeting decided to convene a special session of the Diet on March 20th for a period of three weeks. The Ministry of Finance has already drafted the budget for 1936 and 1937, to be submitted to the Diet, with total expenditures of 2,295,000,000 yen, an increase of 17,000,000 yen compared to the figures that were not passed by the Diet before its dissolution. The amount of bonds to be issued to cover the budget deficit will be limited to 700,000,000 yen, also an increase of 20,000,000 yen compared to before. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

British MP Questions Student Demonstrations in Shanghai International Settlement; Eden Says He Has Not Yet Received Report

London: During a meeting of the House of Commons today, Communist MP Gallacher questioned Foreign Secretary Eden about the clashes between students and police in the Shanghai International Settlement during demonstrations held on December 24th of last year against the so-called autonomous movement in North China. He asked how many students were injured, how many were arrested, how many of the injured students were under the age of sixteen, and whether the British-controlled police had the right to suppress demonstrations by ordinary Chinese people protesting against Japan's policy towards China. Foreign Secretary Eden replied that the British government had instructed local British officials to submit a report, but no reply had been received yet. He added that the local police were controlled by the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement, which is an international body composed of fourteen members, five of whom are British, five Chinese, two American, and two Japanese. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

Sacrificial Ceremony to Confucius Held in Hebei's Yuanping City; Song Zheyuan Presides Over Ceremony in Yuanping; All Agencies and Schools on Holiday

Beiping: Today was the spring Ding sacrificial ceremony to Confucius. Before dawn at 5:00 AM, more than 600 participants, all dressed in formal attire, arrived at the temple. At 6:00 AM, the presiding official Song Zheyuan arrived at the temple. The ceremony began at 6:15 AM and concluded at 7:00 AM, after which participants departed. From 1:00 PM, various schools and organizations held their own sacrifices, and the temple was opened for public viewing. All agencies and schools were ordered to have a day off today. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Tianjin: At 6:00 AM on the 25th, Xiao Zhenying led officials from various bureaus under the municipal government to hold the spring Ding sacrificial ceremony to Confucius inside the East Gate. More than 1,000 representatives from agencies, organizations, and students attended. First, Municipal Government Secretary-General Shi Jisheng held a preparatory ceremony at the Chong Sheng Hall. At 6:00 AM, Xiao led the crowd to perform the sacrifice at the Dacheng Hall. The music was ancient and solemn. Afterwards, the school principals led the students to perform separate sacrifices by class. The ceremony concluded at noon. All agencies and schools had a day off on the 25th. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Baoding: The sacrificial ceremony to Confucius was held at 6:00 AM on the 25th, with more than 600 people attending. Zhang Jiyong presided over the ceremony in place of Song Zheyuan, and Tang Fengjia accompanied the ceremony in place of Wan Fulin. Directors of various departments presented offerings. The ceremony was conducted solemnly in accordance with ancient rites. All agencies and schools were given a day off, and sacrificial meat was distributed. The entire city hung flags in celebration. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

Zhangjiakou: The spring Ding sacrificial ceremony to Confucius in Zhangjiakou was held at the Confucius Temple inside Wan at 5:30 AM on the 25th. More than 200 people attended, including leaders of various agencies, section chiefs in civilian positions, and officers with the rank of major or above in military positions. Zhang Zizhong presided over the ceremony, and Yang Zhaogeng, Ke Changsi, Zhang Lisheng, and Ma Xianfu accompanied the ceremony. The ceremony concluded at 7:00 AM, followed by more than 1,000 students from various schools performing separate sacrifices by class, which was extremely solemn. The ceremony concluded at 11:00 AM. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

All Highways in Hubei Province Reopen to Traffic

Hankou: The total length of all highways in Hubei Province is more than 3,000 kilometers, with annual revenue of more than one million yuan. Since the major flood last year, most of the roads were destroyed. Subsequently, the Department of Construction, considering the province's financial resources and local transportation needs, successively requested the provincial government to discuss and decide on repairs. Nearly half a year has passed, and all highways have now been reopened to traffic. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

Bandits Rob Fuquan Bus, Kidnapping More Than Twenty Passengers

Xiamen: The Fuquan bus heading to the province was robbed near Changsi Ridge in the vicinity of the provincial capital on the afternoon of the 24th. More than 100 bandits from Gao Xuexun's unit kidnapped more than 20 passengers and injured two. At 8:00 PM, they set fire to the nearby Cang Kou. The security team dispatched a team on the 25th to suppress them. (Special dispatch, 25th)

China and France Consult on Revising Regulations for Yunnan-Vietnam Railway, Sign Agreement; Full Text to be Announced After Approval by Both Governments; Zhang Weici Reports on Process During Memorial Week

Kunming: China and France consulted on revising the regulations for the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway and other attachments. After more than two months of efforts and sincere consultations by both sides, twelve articles and five resolutions were finalized and formally signed at the Foreign Affairs Office on the 20th. The resolutions can be implemented immediately by the railway company. The articles will be officially announced and implemented after approval by both governments. On the morning of the 24th, the Provincial Steering Committee held a memorial week and specially invited representative Zhang Weici to report on the process of revising the regulations and the content of the revisions, which lasted about one and a half hours and was quite detailed. More than 2,000 attendees, including representatives from various agencies, organizations, and schools, were pleased with the satisfactory resolution. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

Regular China-France Airmail Service; Shanghai Mail Arrives in London in Just Ten Days, Setting Record

London: After the airmail service jointly operated by China and France officially commenced on the 13th of this month, the first batch of mail sent from Shanghai has arrived at Croydon Airport here in just over ten days, setting a new record for the fastest delivery of mail between Shanghai and London. It is expected to be shortened in the future. This mail was transported by aircraft belonging to China National Aviation Corporation from Shanghai to Hanoi, Vietnam, and then transferred to aircraft of Air France for transportation to Europe. After arriving at the port of Marseille in France yesterday, it was transported here today. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

Minutes of Executive Yuan Meeting; Xu Qingfu Appointed Civil Affairs Commissioner of Zhejiang; Regulations for Commercial Attachés Revised and Approved; Funding for Mongolian Affairs Council Approved; Donation of 20,000 Yuan to Zhashen Temple in Tibet

Nanjing: The Executive Yuan held its 251st regular meeting on the morning of the 25th, attended by Chiang Kai-shek, Kong Xiangxi, Chiang Tso-pin, Chen Shuren, Huang Musong, He Yingqin, Wang Shijie, Liu Ruiheng, Zhang Qun, Wu Dingchang, Chen Shaokuan, Zhang Jia'ao, and chaired by Chiang Kai-shek.

Matters Discussed: Minister of Interior Chiang, Minister of Industry Wu, and Director of the National Health Administration Liu reported on the review of the draft Mining Law. After discussing and revising the original articles one by one, the revised draft was submitted for review and approval. Resolution: Approved as revised and sent to the Central Political Committee. Minister of Industry Wu presented a request to designate commercial representatives stationed abroad into two categories: Commercial Attachés and Commercial Commissioners, and to revise the regulations for Commercial Commissioners stationed abroad to be Regulations for Commercial Attachés stationed abroad for review and record. Resolution: Approved as revised and submitted to the government for record. The five ministries of Interior, Finance, Industry, Education, and Communications, and the National Health Administration reported on the review of the 1936 local revenue and expenditure budget of the Weihaiwei Administrative Office for review and approval. Resolution: Approved according to the review opinions. Chairman Huang of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission presented a request approved by Director Yan to allocate funds for the Sui Province Mongolian Local Autonomy Guidance Office. Resolution: Approved. Funding is 10,000 yuan per month. Chairman Huang of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission presented a request that as the Tibetan Lungtu Jiacuo came to Beijing to express his gratitude, and his accompanying mission was to raise funds for Zhashen Temple, whether the government could donate some funds in addition to private donations to show respect for Buddhism. Resolution: The central government will allocate 20,000 yuan (The President will donate an additional 5,000 yuan).

Appointments and Removals: Huang Shaoxiong, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and concurrently Civil Affairs Commissioner, should be relieved of his concurrent post as Civil Affairs Commissioner. Xu Qingfu is appointed as a member of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and concurrently Civil Affairs Commissioner. Resolution: Approved. Yan Xishan, Director of the Sui Province Mongolian Local Autonomy Guidance Office, telegraphed requesting that Shi Huayan be appointed as Counselor of the office. Resolution: Approved. Zhang Ji resigned from the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, which was approved. Members Zhang Biguo and Chen Bingguang were removed from their posts due to other appointments. Zhang Ximan, Qiu Jia, and Ma Hetian were appointed as members of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission. Resolution: Approved. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

Nanjing: The Ministry of Industry plans to establish Commercial Attachés stationed abroad, with eight articles in the regulations. The regulations, which were approved at the Executive Yuan meeting on the morning of the 25th, divide Commercial Attachés into two categories: Commercial Attachés and Commercial Commissioners, with the same duties: 1. Investigate and report on the financial, transportation, tax, and general industrial situation of the host country; 2. Promote and publicize domestic products; 3. Matters assigned by the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; 4. Matters entrusted by the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry; 5. Investigation matters requested by domestic industrial organizations; 6. Other matters related to various industries. As for the selection of Commercial Attachés to Japan, the Ministry is currently searching for candidates and will submit a decision to the Executive Yuan in the near future so that they can go abroad at the same time as Xu Shiying. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

In addition to private donations, he submitted a request to the Executive Yuan for a donation. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Ice Flowing Slightly Outside Dagukou; Aircraft Rescue Plan Formulated; Icebreaker Carries Coal and Food for Relief; Zhengji Company Suffers Huge Losses

Tianjin: On the 25th, the wind direction at Dagukou still turned to the northwest, and the situation was slightly better. Zhengji Company's Anli wheel, due to the flowing and partially melting ice between Tanggu and Dagu, risked leaving Tanggu for Shanghai at 5:00 AM and arrived at Sally Di Island outside the port in the afternoon. Jin Navigation Company's Changan wheel, which had been trapped outside the port for half a month and was short of water, entered the port through the ice early on the 25th and arrived at Sally Di Island in the afternoon. The two ships telegraphed the Tianjin shipping industry one after another, reporting that the ice outside the port was loosening, but because the wind was not strong, the flow was very small. If the weather is warm tomorrow and the day after, the ships trapped by the ice can gradually escape. Jin Navigation Company's Yongting wheel telegraphed Tianjin on the 25th that the ship was blown by the wind to the beach outside Dagukou on the night of the 24th, and the wings and rudder were broken and could not move. It was extremely dangerous and requested rapid rescue. The navigation company sent the Tianxing icebreaker early on the 25th, carrying a large amount of coal, water, and food, to rescue the ship outside the port and to provide coal and food to the Gan Zhou, Shun Li, and other ships in distress near Heigu. It did not return at night. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Tianjin: The ice in Qinhuangdao is severely frozen, and the number of Chinese and foreign passenger and cargo ships trapped inside and outside the port has reached sixteen. The Xin Taiping and Jilin ships are frozen outside the port, and coal and food have run out. Repeated telegrams for assistance have gone unanswered. Goods on the docks are piling up because they cannot be transported. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Tianjin: The Ministry of Communications telegraphed the Tianjin Maritime Affairs Bureau that the usual fee for Eurasian aircraft is 800 yuan per hour, but in order to rescue the ships trapped by ice, which is a charitable act, it is allowed to be reduced to 200 yuan, nominally for gasoline costs. The Douglas aircraft, which was originally scheduled to come to Tianjin at 12:30 PM on the 25th, changed to 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM on the 26th due to cloudy weather. The municipal government dispatched Liu Dongxuan to assist Maritime Affairs Bureau Director Pan Yaoxiang in taking care of the aircraft at that time. The aircraft's tasks include: dropping food on the trapped ships, surveying the ice situation, planning rescue measures for the ships in distress, and flying to Qinhuangdao to deliver food to the ships in distress there. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Qingdao: Zhengji Shipping Company of Qingdao has six ships trapped in Dagu, including Zeng Li, Shun Li, Feng Li, Chang Li, An Li, and Cheng Li, with losses reaching 400,000 yuan. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Tianjin: The Ministry of Communications telegraphed the Tianjin Maritime Affairs Bureau, approving the dispatch of Eurasian Airlines' large Douglas aircraft from Ping to Tianjin to carry food to the ships in distress outside Dagukou. It is scheduled to arrive in Tianjin on the morning of the 26th and fly outside the port at 10:00 AM to survey the situation of the ships and drop food, and to fly low along the Bohai Bay to deliver food to the ships trapped in the water there. The rental fee is waived, and only the gasoline fee of 200 yuan per hour is charged. The shipping industry rushed to prepare a large amount of dry food tonight and sent eleven representatives from the Chinese and foreign shipping industry to accompany the aircraft. Xiao dispatched Social Affairs Bureau Director Liu Dongxuan to assist in the relief of the ships in distress and spent his own money to bear the gasoline costs of the Douglas aircraft. (Special dispatch, 25th)

Tianjin: Tianjin Navigation Company's Tianxing wheel loaded coal, water, and food at 11:00 AM on the 25th and sailed to Dagukou to supply the frozen ships, arriving at about 5:00 PM. At the same time, it also carried representatives from various shipping companies to inspect the actual situation in order to rescue them. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

Hankou Customs Brokerage Asks for the Cancellation of the Six-Wheel Bureau's Notary Office

Hankou - Recently, the six shipping companies of Hankou - China Merchants, Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Sanbei, Jijiang, and Nisshin - have jointly organized a notary office for the export of goods. All export goods must be measured and weighed with the skin by the notary office. However, the customs brokerage industry is quite opposed to this, because in the export goods, such as pickled vegetables transported from the upper reaches, they are all packed in earthen jars. The weight of each earthen jar ranges from seven catties to twenty-five catties. If they are weighed with the skin, the merchants will be unable to bear it. In the future, goods from the upper reaches will inevitably be directly transported to Shanghai, and the customs brokerage industry in Hankou will be greatly affected. Therefore, they have sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting that it forward a letter to the six companies to quickly cancel the notary office. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

International Commercial Telegraph - Reuter's Report on Commodity Market Conditions, February 25th

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today's gold price fell two pence to 140 shillings and ten pence.

London Silver Bar: Today's silver market is stable. The spot price is 19 pence 75, and the futures price is 19 pence 6875, both down one two five. India has made some purchases, and the market has a slight general selling trend.

Munterly Silver: Today's futures are quite stable. The March opening fell ten pounds, to 44.65.

Exchange Rates

Sterling/Dollar: This morning, the London foreign exchange market opened with a slight increase in the price of the pound, which then fell. At 10:30, the sterling/dollar exchange rate was four dollars, ninety-nine cents, nine three seven five, which was one eight seven five higher than yesterday's US/British closing price. At 11:00, it fell two five, and then continued to fall two five, to four dollars, ninety-nine cents, four three seven five.

Securities

New York: The market opened this morning with slight differences, but then the buying momentum revived, and prices rose uniformly. Automobile, department store, and railway stocks all rose due to purchases. Metals, steel, and utility stocks were all sluggish. The market prices of New York securities are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: The opening this morning was stable, but the price rose due to good buying momentum. Recently, it has been more stable. The industry is slightly active. Developments in Washington remain a very important factor affecting the market.

Liverpool Cotton: Today's futures are stable. At 1:00 PM, the May price rose one pound to 5.71.

Chicago Wheat: The Chicago wheat and grain market this morning remained sluggish and lacked interest. At 11:00, the wheat price was 99.25 and the grain price was 60.125, both the same as yesterday's price.

Liverpool Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market opened stably this morning. Sellers were firm, resulting in better-than-expected prices. Later, prices soared due to strong buying. At 1:00 PM, the March price rose six two five, to six shillings and two pence. The current price remained firm.

Rubber

London: The market opened this morning, and the market was not very active. Later, prices stabilized. At 1:00 PM, the transaction price for April 6 was 7 pence 4375, the same as the supervised closing price.

New York: The market situation today is weak, because the labor strike in Akron has not yet been resolved, and the Rubber Restriction Committee failed to issue a communique after closing today. The March opening fell seven pounds, to 15.53. The market situation has been stable since then. The market prices of New York goods are listed on the left.
