Japan Expresses Deliberation on the Eastern Hebei Puppet Organization. Tada Freely Discusses Issues in Hebei and Chahar in Peiping. Chen Zhongfu and Doihara Continue to Exchange Opinions.

Peiping Correspondence: Regarding the Eastern Hebei incident, after nearly a week of consultations, it is heard that the Japanese side has indicated that the issue of abolishing the puppet organization can be considered in the long term. At the same time, the Japanese side has made some claims regarding the original name of "Demilitarized Zone" after the abolition of the Eastern Hebei puppet organization. After negotiation, it was agreed to leave it for the second step of consultation. Doihara was scheduled to visit Song Zheyuan on the morning of the 24th for consultations.

Tada Hayao, commander of the Japanese garrison in Tianjin, spoke to reporters at the Fushang Hall on the 23rd regarding various issues in Hebei and Chahar. According to him, "I very much hope that the 'merger' of the Eastern Hebei Autonomous Government and the Hebei-Chahar Political Council will be realized. However, there is a difference between the two sides, namely that the Eastern Hebei Autonomous Government is touted as being anti-communist, while the establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council is a lifeline with the Nanjing government, so their purposes are slightly different. They can only merge if the two sides reach the same level. Chairman Song is currently working hard on reform, striving for the happiness of the people. If the reform is successful in the future, the merger with the Eastern Hebei organization will naturally be easy. Regarding the Zhangbei incident, our army has not interfered much. The Japanese Kwantung Army negotiated with the chairman of Chahar Province, and the Chahar side has agreed to allow Li Shouxin's Security Brigade to be stationed there. Therefore, the details of the agreement between the Japanese Kwantung Army stationed in Chahar and the Chahar side are not known because they are not within the scope of the jurisdiction of the Japanese garrison in Tianjin. In short, the Japanese side has absolutely no intention of occupying it, and even less of merging the Eastern Hebei and Chahar areas into Manchukuo. This is what I, as the commander, can assert. I hope that your country, from top to bottom, will deeply believe in this intention. It should be known that Sino-Japanese friendship is by no means just lip service, let alone empty talk. What is painful is that Sino-Japanese relations are worse after the Russo-Japanese War than before the Russo-Japanese War. China and Japan should not only blame others, but should also blame themselves. The path to friendship should be initiated by both sides, and both sides have mutual responsibilities. If we want to improve relations, both sides have responsibilities to bear. China and Japan should abandon the concept of being right ourselves and wronging others and seek mutual understanding. Future relations should seek new paths. I think the Communist Party is like a flood and a beast. One wrong step will lead to eternal regret. Doihara, the chief of the special agency of the Japanese Kwantung Army stationed in Panjin, does not have the mission of conducting Sino-Japanese negotiations with the Peiping authorities. I have not yet received a report on the increase of Japanese troops stationed in North China, and I have only seen it in the newspaper. I have no trip to Zhangjiakou. I took a plane to browse the Ping-Sui line before, but only looked down at Datong from the plane. In fact, I did not go to Datong. Bailingmiao is far away in Mongolia and has some relationship with the Japanese Kwantung Army. I have not been there recently. Our country has a very deep misunderstanding with your country, and I would like to talk to you about this. My impression of coming to Peiping this time is that Sino-Japanese relations have improved. For example, the anti-Japanese movement has calmed down on the surface, but the lives of the common people are worse than in the seventh and eighth years of the Republic of China. The commercial depression has intensified. As for the Hebei-Chahar Political Council and the various committees under it, the matter of hiring Japanese people to serve as technical consultants was entrusted by Chairman Song. At this time, I have introduced them to the Japanese side on behalf of him, but I have not yet received a reply. Furthermore, there is no response to the number of consultants and their future tasks." etc.

Regarding the solution of various issues in Hebei and Chahar, after the Japanese side put forward concrete opinions, the parties concerned have been carefully considering methods for days. Chen Zhongfu, chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, visited Doihara at the Fushang Hall at 10:00 AM on the 22nd to exchange views. Tada, commander of the Japanese garrison in Tianjin, was also present. They talked for half an hour before Chen left. That afternoon, at 5:15 PM, Chen took the Beining Railway train to Tianjin to discuss everything with Tianjin Mayor Xiao Zhenying. The Foreign Affairs Committee is scheduled to hold a meeting at the end of this month. Due to the Japanese side's opinion, it is hoped that after the newly appointed Japanese Ambassador to China, Arita, takes office, before the Nanjing meeting is held, the Hebei-Chahar issue will come to an end. Doihara also plans to leave Peiping in the middle of next month and return to Changchun for a trip. As for all the issues in Eastern Hebei and Northern Chahar, whether they can be resolved as we hope, or whether they will maintain the status quo, there should be a factual demonstration within the next two weeks. In addition, Yagami Toshiyasu, chief of staff of the Japanese garrison in Tianjin, visited Song Zheyuan at Wuyiku Hutong at 11:00 AM on the 22nd. After talking for half an hour, he left and returned to Tianjin at 1:00 PM that afternoon. (23rd)

Gansu Provincial Government: Afforestation Plan Along the Yellow River: Afforestation along the Yellow River is a vital policy for the Northwest; the provincial government plans a five-year implementation plan.

Lanzhou Dispatch: The provincial government considers the security of the Yellow River through afforestation to be a crucial current policy. It instructed the Department of Construction to formulate an implementation plan, which the department drafted and submitted to the provincial government for referral to the Ministry of Industries for review. The original draft plan is outlined below:

General Overview of the Yellow River Basin

The largest tributaries of the Yellow River in this province are the Wei River and the Tao River. Afforestation along the riverbanks can be carried out in cooperation with the Forestry Bureau of Shaanxi Province in the future. The source of the Tao River has rich natural forests, so the Tao River carries very little sediment. In the future, this province should plan to increase afforestation and protect the natural forests in the Tao and Min areas. Speaking of the Yellow River itself, the Yellow River in Gansu Province passes through six counties, including Linxia, Yongjing, , Yuzhong, Jingyuan, and Jingtai. It is not yet possible to determine how much land is suitable for afforestation along the riverbanks in each of these counties because no on-site surveys have been conducted. The areas suitable for afforestation reported by each county are listed below: Yuzhong has 1,580 mu of land suitable for afforestation along the riverbanks; Jingyuan has 2,800 mu of land suitable for afforestation along the riverbanks; the riverbank in this Lan area is 110 li long (no report of the number of mu suitable for afforestation); the riverbank in Yongjing is 45 li long (no report of the number of mu suitable for afforestation); the riverbank in Linxia is 10 li long, mostly rocky cliffs, not suitable for planting trees. The mu numbers reported by the above counties are accurate. A detailed survey is still necessary when afforestation is carried out in the future. The riverbank in Gaolan County is more than 110 li long, and the land suitable for afforestation should not be small. Therefore, this plan cannot specify the afforestation locations, but only divides the time and location to serve as the work procedure.

Measures for Implementing Afforestation

After years of natural disasters and man-made calamities in this province, financial difficulties have reached their peak. There is no special organization for afforestation, and there are no dedicated funds for afforestation expenses. Although there were various forestry plans in the past, they were not implemented due to insufficient financial resources. Therefore, this plan must narrow the scope, focusing only on the banks of the main Yellow River basin to ensure it is realistic. Appoint a specialist to guide the implementation of the work. Establishing a specialized agency would be costly and would slow down progress. It is planned that the Department of Construction will select one specialist who is proficient in both forestry and water conservancy to be responsible for managing the Yellow River and afforestation matters. This year, he will be sent to various places along the Yellow River to conduct an on-site survey, formulate an afforestation plan, and submit it to the provincial government for approval and implementation. Then, the specialist will guide the implementation. To promote the implementation of afforestation, the Yellow River basin in this province starts from the border between Gansu and Qinghai and extends eastward to the border with Ningxia. The river meanders for about 900 li. It is impossible to carry out afforestation at the same time, and there is no way to obtain a large number of saplings. It is planned to divide the main Yellow River into three sections: from Jishi Pass to Hekou as one section, from Hekou to Jingyuan as one section, and from Jingyuan to (Fosi Temple) as one section. Each section will have a Yellow River Afforestation Office, named after the location. For example, the Hekou section will be named the Yellow River Hekou Section Office, and so on. Each section will have one technician and two forest workers to handle afforestation matters within that section according to the plan. The completion period is set at five years. The annual business operations will be detailed in the next section. The main tasks of each afforestation office are that the climate in this province is dry, and it often does not rain for two or three months in spring and summer, which is not suitable for afforestation. Although the soil near the river is moist, it can still be used for some cutting afforestation, but the rest still needs to be planted with trees. Starting with cultivating seedlings, the main task of the thorn-growing office is to implement a portion of cutting afforestation every year and cultivate a suitable amount of seedlings to prepare for planting trees in the third year. The business allocation: Before the afforestation implementation plan is determined, this plan is intended to be easy to explain and a number is temporarily set as a rough estimate. Each section is 300 li long, and both banks are 600 li. It is tentatively set to plant 10 mu of trees per li, and each section should plant 6,000 mu of trees. If five years are used as the completion period, an average of 1,200 mu must be afforested each year. The funds for this plan are in accordance with the original plan of the Ministry of Industry for afforestation along the Yellow River. There is already an amount of 24,000 yuan. If one mu of afforestation costs 20 yuan according to the local conditions in this province, only 1,200 mu can be afforested. In order to use the people's service, the leveling, irrigation, and cuttings are all done by the public providing labor and giving subsidies. The technicians will work with the local county government and local Baojia to coordinate the implementation. All the planted forests will be handed over to the local county government for safekeeping as security forests after planting. All expenses can be saved. It is estimated that 65,706 yuan of afforestation expenses will be required in five years. In addition to the 24,000 yuan, there is still a shortfall of 41,706 yuan. Therefore, if the amount is insufficient after two years, the provincial government will need to continue to raise funds to support it. The detailed method of requisitioning labor will be submitted for approval during implementation.

Work Progress Steps

The progress of this Yellow River afforestation work is scheduled for five years, from 1936 to 1940. In the first year, willows and poplars will be planted on both sides of the Yellow River. The distance between the two trees is about one zhang. There are 200 trees per mu, and each section afforests 400 mu. The three sections together account for 1,200 mu. In the same year, 7,200 mu will be afforested in 1938, with 240 trees per mu. In that year, each section should cultivate 576,000 seedlings, and the three sections should prepare a total of 1,728,000 seedlings. In the second year, the three sections together will carry out cutting afforestation on 1,200 mu, but the 1,728,000 seedlings cultivated in the previous year should be transplanted to other places for the purpose of preparing for afforestation of 2,400 mu in 1939. In that year, each section should cultivate 192,000 seedlings, and the three sections should cultivate a total of 576,000 seedlings. In the third year, the three sections together will carry out cutting afforestation on 1,200 mu. Because the 1,728,000 seedlings cultivated in the first year have grown, each section should plant 2,400 mu of trees according to the previous plan, and the three sections should afforest a total of 7,200 mu to prepare for afforestation in 1939. Each section should transplant 572,000 old seedlings, and the three sections should transplant a total of 1,728,000 seedlings. Also, to prepare for afforestation of 2,400 mu in 1940, each section should cultivate 192,000 seedlings, and the three sections should cultivate a total of 576,000 seedlings. In the fourth year, the three sections together will carry out cutting afforestation on 1,200 mu and plant trees on 2,400 mu, but the seedlings cultivated in the previous year are easy to grow. Each section should transplant 192,000 old seedlings, and the three sections should transplant a total of 576,000 seedlings. In the fifth year, the three sections together will carry out cutting afforestation on 1,200 mu and plant trees on 2,400 mu. The total afforestation area within five years is 18,000 mu, with 4,080,000 trees.

Rough Budget Estimate

In the first year (1936), the travel expenses required for the afforestation guidance specialist to conduct surveys and inspections were 2,000 yuan. Each section has one technician, and the living expenses and office expenses are 50 yuan per month. The total cost for the three sections for the whole year is 1,800 yuan, forest police 720 yuan, purchasing 240,000 willow and poplar tree stumps, at a price of 1 cent per stump, a total of 240 yuan, seed costs for the three sections totaling 600 yuan, digging holes and planting for cutting afforestation costs 1.5 yuan per mu, totaling 1,800 yuan for 1,200 mu, seedling cultivation and irrigation costs for the three sections totaling 1,728 yuan, requisitioning labor costs 600 yuan, renting 30 mu of nursery land for each section, with a rent of 10 yuan per mu, the annual rent for the three sections of nursery land is 900 yuan, the monthly rent for each section is 10 yuan, and the rent for the three sections is 300 yuan. The total afforestation cost for the first year is 12,908 yuan. In the second year (1937), the specialist's travel expenses are 1,500 yuan, the technician's living expenses are 1,800 yuan, the forest police are 720 yuan, the stump fee is 2,400 yuan, the seed fee is 450 yuan, the transplanting old seedlings and irrigating new seedlings fee is 2,300 yuan, the technician's activity fee is 600 yuan, the nursery land rent is 900 yuan, the rent is 300 yuan, and the cutting afforestation subsidy fee is 1,800 yuan, totaling 12,800 yuan. In the third year (1938), the specialist's travel expenses are 1,000 yuan, the technician's living expenses are 1,800 yuan, the forest police are 720 yuan, the tree stump fee is 2,400 yuan, the cutting afforestation subsidy fee is 1,800 yuan, the seed fee is 300 yuan, the tree planting subsidy fee is 8,200 yuan, the transplanting old seedlings and irrigating new seedlings fee is 1,152 yuan, and the technician's activity fee is 600 yuan, totaling 18,232 yuan. In the fourth year (1939), the specialist's travel expenses are 500 yuan, the technician's living expenses are 1,800 yuan, the forest police are 720 yuan, the tree stump fee is 2,400 yuan, the cutting afforestation subsidy fee is 1,800 yuan, the tree planting subsidy is 2,400 yuan, the transplanting old seedlings and irrigating new seedlings fee is 570 yuan, the technician's activity fee is 600 yuan, and the rent is 360 yuan, totaling 11,150 yuan. In the fifth year (1940), the specialist's travel expenses are 500 yuan, the technician's living expenses are 1,800 yuan, the forest police are 720 yuan, the tree stump fee is 2,400 yuan, the cutting afforestation subsidy fee is 1,800 yuan, the tree planting subsidy fee is 2,400 yuan, the technician's activity fee is 600 yuan, and the rent is 360 yuan, totaling 10,580 yuan. The total afforestation cost for five years is 65,706 yuan.

Pinghan Railway Bureau: Construction of the Xuyu Branch Line: Surveying Work Nearing Completion

Kaifeng Dispatch: The proposal to build a railway between Xuchang and Yuxian in Henan Province has been around for a long time. In 1933, the gentry and merchants of Xuchang and Yu counties formed a preparatory committee and hired engineers to start surveying the route and drawing up charts, gradually making it concrete. However, it was abandoned due to the economic depression in Xuchang and Yu and the bankruptcy of the rural areas, making it difficult to raise shares. This year, the Pinghan Railway Bureau was ordered by the Ministry to build the Xuyu branch line and sent Tan Zhendong, deputy chief of the bureau's engineering section, to lead more than ten employees to carry out surveying. It is reported that Tan and others departed from Xuchang more than ten days ago and the work along the way has been very smooth. Bridges and culverts have been surveyed and completed. They have now arrived in Yuxian to survey and map the South Gate Station, the end point of the road. It is planned to be at the Zhongfeng Coal Mine in Majiadong in the Seventh District of Yuxian. The entire line will have four stations: Xuchang, Quandian, Yuxian, and Majiadong. In the future, if needed, small stations may be added in Lingjing and Quanhepup. (23rd)

Datong: Robbery of the Bank of China's Agency: Loss of More Than 19,000 Gold Yuan

Wuhu Dispatch: Datong Town, located between Wuhu and the province, is adjacent to the Yangtze River. Before the Wuhu-Tunxi Highway was opened to traffic, it was the gateway to Huizhou, Tongling, Qingyang, and Jiuhua Mountain. It is also one of the largest market towns in Anhui Province besides Wuhu. Therefore, the Bank of China in Wuhu specially established an office in the town's Lifeng Money Shop, called the Bank of China Datong Agency, to balance the daily business income, which was also very large. Unexpectedly, Wuhu just received a telegram that the Datong Agency was processing the day's business statistics at 7:30 p.m. on the 23rd when five or six bandits suddenly broke into the shop, holding weapons and driving the staff into a corner. Four bandits went to the office and forced the agency's manager, Zhou Xueqin, to hand over the key to the iron cabinet and immediately shot Zhou in the head. Zhou immediately fainted. The bandits then shot another employee, seized the key, opened the iron cabinet, and robbed a total of more than 19,000 yuan in legal tender, which they put into a rattan suitcase they had brought with them. Then they gathered to the back and When a bandit on the outside lookout shouted "Good" (meaning the predetermined password), the five bandits and others grabbed the and rushed out the door. The whole process did not take five or six minutes, and their actions were very agile. At that time, all the employees saw Manager Zhou being shot by the bandits and were almost frightened out of their wits. They didn't know where the bandits had fled. Zhou slightly regained consciousness, and the employees dared to divide and rush to report to the local Public Security Bureau and the Third District Office. Zhou also struggled to get up, pressed his hand on the wound, and ran painfully to the Public Security Bureau to briefly report the truth of the robbery at that time. Upon receiving the report, the police station immediately dispatched all the police and militia teams to pursue the bandits. The Hai'e torpedo boat of the Navy, which was stationed on the Datong River, also announced a river ban and hired two Anwu small ferries to sail to Meigeng upstream and Henggang downstream to search for the bandits. However, the bandits had already escaped without a trace with the stolen goods. Manager Zhou suffered serious injuries to his head and has been hospitalized for treatment. The Wuhu branch of the Bank of China specially sent Deputy Director Nan to Tong on the morning of the 24th to investigate the incident. (24th)

Overview of Nanjing's Firefighting Services: Fire Brigades and Firefighting Associations Complement Each Other; Automatic Telephones are Detrimental to Transmitting Alarms; There are Nineteen Firefighting Organizations in the City

Nanjing Dispatch: Since Nanjing became the capital, the population has been increasing day by day. In 1927, the city had only more than 360,000 people. Recently, according to the Police Department, it has reached more than one million, almost tripling. Whether the firefighting strength of the city is in direct proportion to the increase in population is a question. Here is a brief survey of its outline.

Generally, firefighting organizations can be divided into two categories: regular firefighters and volunteer firefighters. The so-called regular firefighters are paid, while volunteer firefighters are unpaid. In other words, regular firefighters are a fixed organization and receive a certain amount of remuneration. Volunteer firefighters are temporarily assembled only after an incident occurs, and return to their original positions afterward without receiving any remuneration. As of now, there are a total of nineteen firefighting organizations in Nanjing, including six fire brigades and thirteen firefighting associations. The distribution is as follows: one fire brigade each in the East, South, North, Central, Xiaguan, and Pukou districts; three firefighting associations in the East District, one in the South District, three in the West District, two in the North District, three in the Central District, and one in the Xiaguan District.

Regarding the actual situation of Nanjing's firefighting organization, I had the honor of hearing the details from Wang Ji, captain of the Fire Police Brigade, and Xu Hanquan, the gentleman from the First Firefighting Association in the East District. First, let me describe Nanjing's regular firefighters. According to Wang, the fire brigade is under the jurisdiction of the Capital Police Department, so its source of funding is only a part of the police administrative expenses. Until now, there has been no specific funding. Therefore, the rise and fall of firefighting organizations often depends on whether the past principals attach importance to this kind of undertaking as the standard. Director Wang (Gu Pan) has not been in office for long and there have been no changes. During Director Chen (Zhuo)'s tenure, he made every effort to reorganize. At that time, there were a total of eighteen fire police teams. Later, six teams were cut, and the savings were used to add firefighting equipment. The new fire engines have been increased to six. At this time, the funding has not increased, but the firefighting strength has increased a lot.

Also, since the adoption of automatic telephones, the general public naturally feels convenient, but from the perspective of firefighting, it is a huge loss. During the period when magneto or common battery telephones were used, in the event of a fire alarm, all kinds of important calls had to be temporarily stopped and transmitted first. Now, the use of machine calls has lost its flexible function and has led to delays, because it is in units of fifty. Among these fifty, only ten can be connected at the same time. When we use the telephone, we often hear a busy tone, ("buzzing sound") the reason is that we have not yet obtained the opportunity to talk. Just imagine how can we suffer this kind of unexpected delay when a fire occurs? Regarding the remedy, after consulting with the telephone bureau, there is only one method of installing a dedicated line, but the cost is too high and it is practically impossible. Now, another telephone is installed in the team headquarters, specifically for external to internal calls. In this way, only one opportunity to talk has been reduced, and the effect is very limited.

There are two watchtowers in Nanjing: Chengnan is the Zhonghua Gate tower, and Chengbei is the Drum Tower tower. In addition, police stations in various places are also responsible for reporting. After the Firefighting Headquarters obtains the above information, it immediately dispatches the team on one side and transmits the news to various fire brigades and firefighting associations on the other side. As for civil notification, it can also be heavy at any time through the method of interrogation.

The First Firefighting Association in the East District is a business-run organization and is, needless to say, a volunteer firefighting organization. The association's expenses are donated by merchants, but the firefighters are paid salaries. At the same time, they also stay in the association all day long so that they can be dispatched at any time. In this way, it is essentially a regular firefighting organization. According to Xu, the association has a history of more than 100 years. During the Qing Dynasty, it was the Yongping Water Dragon Bureau. In 1929, it changed to a pump machine and was called the Yongping Firefighting Association. In April 1931, it was divided into the East District. In 1932, it accumulated funds to purchase a fire engine. This was the beginning of Nanjing's own modern fire engines. Up to now, the firefighting association has added nine vehicles, plus the six fire brigades. There are already fifteen vehicles in the city. In addition, there are gas cylinders (pumps), which are divided into towed, fixed, and mounted types. In addition to each of the nineteen firefighting organizations in the city having one, the Beilu Fire Brigade has two, for a total of twenty. The general number of firefighting equipment in the city is roughly as follows.

In the spring of 1929, a fire broke out in Zhangfuyuan in Chengnan during the day. Later, it spread to the Inner Bridge. The fire raged across the river, burning on both sides, and spread to the area of ​​Shengping Bridge, all the way to the former site of Shangyuan County Office, now the site of the Poor Children's Education Institute. A total of 200 households and shops were burned down. The fire started at lunchtime and was extinguished in the evening. After this major fire, the citizens of Nanjing almost changed color when talking about police, and were very vigilant, especially businessmen, who were more concerned. According to Xu, the strength of the fire brigade was limited at that time, and the association was still using the old-fashioned pump. It goes without saying that the other firefighting associations were even worse. In addition, the municipality was immature at the time and the streets were narrow. Every time a fire broke out, it often led to a major disaster. The merchants learned this lesson and unanimously and enthusiastically donated funds to purchase modern firefighting equipment. The First Firefighting Association in the East District purchased a modern gas cylinder under such circumstances. Since then, after several years of operation, the strength of firefighting in the city has reached today's state.

Songjiang: Improvement of the Provincial Security Team

In order to improve the security teams in the province, the Provincial Security Office has drafted an improvement outline, which has been approved for implementation. Regarding the security brigades stationed in various counties, the county magistrates who served concurrently as the brigade commanders will no longer serve concurrently from March onwards. The original major brigade adjutants will be reassigned as brigade commanders and will be under the jurisdiction of the district security commander. However, the county magistrates still have the power to command. Regarding the funding part, which was previously allocated by the county government under the county's funding items, the province has now directly issued a payment order to establish a district treasury. The security funds of each county will be allocated to the district treasury on a monthly basis for unified collection and expenditure. It is reported that the Mei-Jin plan is about to be implemented.

Spring Cold Suddenly Snows

Since the beginning of spring, it has been raining continuously, and the coldness has not diminished in the cold winter. The spring cold is bleak, and the spring is rarely felt. Unexpectedly, a strong wind suddenly broke out on the night of the 24th, and on the morning of the 25th at about 3:00 a.m., snow fell, followed by snow pellets. Spring crops were damaged, and farmers were worried.

Villager Robbed, Old Mother Grieved

Ma Tugen's family, the second household in the second Jia of the Erbao of Jingnantang Township in the Eighth District, is in a difficult situation. Unexpectedly, they were also coveted by bandits. At about 1:00 a.m. on the 22nd, eight robbers who spoke with a strong accent broke into the back window and wounded the householder's mother, Zhang, in the right corner of her forehead. The blood flowed like a pillar. They continued to rob, carrying and fleeing. The clothes and rice that were robbed were not reported afterward. Niu Wanqi, the patrol officer of the Ninth Substation, heard about it, and after personally conducting an on-site investigation, he reported to the county bureau requesting the arrest of the thieves.

Water Patrol Team Cracks Down on Drug Trafficking

The re-registration of opium smokers in this county has expired. A general inspection has been ordered to all districts and water and land public security agencies to ensure that there are no omissions. County Chief Li recently received a tip that there was drug trafficking in Huangqiao and other places in the county. He ordered Fei Gongxia, the captain of the water patrol team, to investigate. Captain Fei personally led the second patrol officer to Huangqiao, Qibao, Sijing, and other places, but found nothing. Yesterday, he went to Xinzhuang and found Li Huogen, Qian Ahu, and Zhang Guanming in an empty house at No. 1, Jia, Bao 1 in the Fourth, injecting morphine. They were all covered with needle scars and looked haggard. After strict interrogation, they confessed that Sheng Hongru's house, No. 10, Jia 4, Bao 7, was selling morphine. He immediately went to the address to arrest him and found four small packets of morphine, an injection needle, a small cup, and a scale on the bed. He immediately brought the witnesses back to Shen and sent them to the county government for legal action.

Cangtai: Fengjiaqiao Qian's Residence Robbed

Fengjiaqiao Town, which belongs to the county, is one of the small towns in the county. There are dozens of residents, and the Qian family is relatively wealthy, so they were coveted by bandits. In the late night of the 24th, more than 20 bandits suddenly came, each holding a weapon, broke open the gate, and robbed several families, including Qian Youpo, Qian Senmei, Qian Tianguan, and Qian Xidong. It is estimated that gold and silver jewelry, banknotes, and foreign money worth more than 5,000 yuan were robbed. Qian Youpo suffered the greatest loss. Jiading: Local Gentleman Zhu Xibai Passes Away

Local gentleman Zhu Xibai (讳寿朋), was a Jinshi in the former Qing Dynasty. His morality and articles were valued by the world. Now, due to his advanced age and weakness, he suddenly developed asthma and died in his residence at No. 29, Gaomenlou, Nanjing, on the 19th of this month, at the age of 68. Zhu was honest and self-disciplined and could be a model for future generations. Yu Hongqi, a member of the Supervisory Yuan, and Ye Chucang, a member of the Central Committee, sent elegiac couplets to show their admiration.

Suzhou: More Than One Inch of Snow Accumulates in Suzhou City

In the past ten days in Suzhou, it has been raining continuously and the weather has been abnormally cold. This morning (25th), the climate suddenly changed and it felt even colder. At about 9:00, snow pellets were mixed in the drizzle. By noon, it was snowing heavily, and within two hours, the snow had accumulated to more than an inch. The city's business district has become even more depressed as a result. It is said that various entertainment venues such as the Beijing Theater and cinemas have been most affected, and their business has plummeted. Other small vendors are also complaining endlessly.

Chamber of Commerce Resolves to Restore the Arbitration Office

The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce had an arbitration office during the era of the General Chamber of Commerce, which was dedicated to mediating commercial disputes. Later, it was abolished invisibly. Because the County Chamber of Commerce has seen that the commercial economy has been sluggish in recent years and that disputes have emerged one after another, once a lawsuit is involved, it often takes years to resolve. In order to avoid the suffering of merchants, the Executive Committee discussed and resolved to restore the Commercial Arbitration Committee yesterday. All organizations are in the process of being drafted. As for the various trade associations, they will also separately organize mediation committees so that if disputes cannot be resolved in the various trade associations, they will be sent to the arbitration association of the Chamber of Commerce for processing.

The Xiangqiao farmers and family in Zhizhang Township were suddenly robbed by twenty or thirty bandits the night before. In addition to two box guns, the weapons used by the bandits included bayonets, axes, etc. They bound the victims, including their wives and daughters, and poured cold water into their mouths and noses to force them to ask where the silver was hidden. As a result, the robbery lasted two hours before they howled and left. In addition to 200 yuan in cash and silver coins, there were also jewelry, clothes, etc., totaling about 1,000 yuan.

Yaogao Baomin Township's Shao Family Robbed

Prison Inmates from Rutai Transferred to Nantong Prison

The High Court is currently transferring one hundred and twenty inmates sentenced to more than three years of imprisonment from various prisons in Rutai to the Fourth Prison of Nantong to fill the vacancies left after the release on parole.

Jiaxing Gathering and Training of Bao Chiefs

The county-wide training of Bao chiefs is now scheduled to begin on March 1st and will last for one month. However, due to the large number of people, the county will first select the younger and stronger ones for training. It has been decided to first select 513 Bao chiefs for the first phase of training. The convening orders have already been issued. All Bao chiefs are required to report by February 28th. However, the Bao chiefs, feeling that the training period is too rushed, have been submitting requests to the county government through the town offices to resign. The county government believes that these Bao chiefs should not be submitting resignation requests at this time to avoid the training, so all requests have been rejected.

County Government Changes Head of Finance Section

Zhang Haoming, the head of the Finance Section of the County Government, has been reassigned to the position of head of the Finance Section of the Jiashan County Government. Therefore, he resigned from the Wang County Magistrate of Jiaxing. As a result, the vacancy for the head of the Finance Section of the Jiaxing County Government has been filled by Sun Zhonglai, the secretary of the County Government, who has been appointed by the county.

Hangzhou Spring Cold and Snow Affect Agricultural Production

The weather in Hangzhou has been unusually cold recently, with a sudden drop in temperature. On the 24th, the Fahrenheit thermometer dropped to 32 degrees. On the morning of the 25th, spring snow fell, melting as it fell, and continued until the afternoon, with the accumulated snow reaching about an inch. The spring cold has become even more severe, with no hope of easing up. According to agricultural experts, this spring snow is harmful to agriculture. Wheat and rapeseed are currently in the developmental stage and are severely affected by the spring freeze, which will inevitably reduce the harvest.

Shaoxing National Service Continues Work

The Shaoxing National Labor Service Project has reached five or six tenths of completion. Work was temporarily suspended due to the end of the lunar year and the rain and snow. Since the beginning of spring, in addition to once mobilizing able-bodied men from the Chengdong and Chengzhong towns to concentrate on the Yue Wangtai to organize the Fushan Project, it is now scheduled to fully mobilize able-bodied men from all the towns in the city starting from the 25th to continue the work. The project will continue to be carried out as originally planned.

Xiaoshan Agricultural Extension Center Robbed by Bandits

The Zhejiang Provincial Agricultural Extension Personnel Training Center in Wenyan, Xiaoshan, was suddenly attacked by seven bandits at around 7:00 PM on the 22nd. They were dressed in short clothes, three of them carrying pistols, and the rest wielding short knives, making a threatening display. They entered the accounting office, ransacked the boxes and cabinets, and stole a deposit book from the Bank of China worth 2,000 yuan, 120 yuan in cash from the labor service fund, and a fur coat belonging to accountant Zeng. After about an hour, they fled towards the Hengzhutang area. It is reported that the center has already reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau for investigation and arrest.

Large Numbers of Refugees Arrive Continuously

In the Xitang area near Guali, Xiaoshan, over 250 refugees from Anhui arrived on the 21st and set up camp at the Xijiang Dao Temple. The town office and the township office came forward to maintain order and distributed rations, ordering them to live in the Jiudun Temple and the Hudu Temple. On the 23rd, over a hundred refugees from Xianglai arrived. The next day, they were accommodated in the Saint Emperor Temple and the Sanguan Temple. Subsequently, they were escorted by the police to the Anchang Yifeng area.

Local News

Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange Auction of Unified Public Bonds Public Notice Stipulates Eight Measures Implemented on the 28th Futures Trading for February to Be Settled Tomorrow Old Bonds to Be Exchanged Starting March 11th

The Board of Directors of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange resolved and announced that the auction of unified public bonds will commence on February 28th, with spot and futures trading for March and April. Eight measures for the auction have been stipulated. The futures for February will be settled tomorrow, and trading has been suspended since yesterday to handle settlement matters. Details are as follows:

Board of Directors Resolves to Commence Auction

The Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, by order of the Ministry of Finance, will auction public bonds and treasury bills starting on February 17th, allowing new purchases but prohibiting new sales. The auction is specifically for the 63 million yuan of futures trading for February, which ended on January 29th, entirely to clear previous accounts and set the settlement date for February 27th. As for the auction of the five types of unified public bonds (A, B, C, D, and E), the Board of Directors of the Exchange has resolved to commence the auction on February 28th. The listings for the unified public bonds have all been prepared, and all preparations have been completed.

Eight Measures Stipulated for Auction

The Exchange issued Public Notice No. 2267 yesterday morning, stating: "Having been resolved by the Board of Directors, the auction of unified public bonds for spot and futures trading in March and April will commence on February 28th. The measures for the auction, as well as the proclamation of the Ministry of Finance and the regulations and repayment schedule for the unified public bonds, are listed below. In addition to informing the brokers' association, this public notice is hereby issued." The measures are as follows: Auction of spot goods and futures trading for March and April will be conducted for the five types of unified public bonds (A, B, C, D, and E). For spot goods, the face value will be in units of 1,000 yuan; for futures trading, the face value will be in units of 5,000 yuan. The method of buying and selling spot goods will be in accordance with Public Notice No. 709 of this Exchange. For futures trading in March and April, both parties must pay 400 yuan in cash and 400 yuan in special certificates for every 10,000 yuan traded. Unified public bonds with a face value of 5,000 yuan can be used interchangeably with bonds with a face value of 1,000 yuan at the time of settlement. These public bonds can be used as substitutes for security deposits and are universally applicable for both buyers and sellers. The price fluctuation of these public bonds will be limited to 4 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. If the limit is exceeded, the auction will be temporarily suspended to handle margin calls. The aforementioned measures will be implemented starting on the 28th of this month.

Public Notice on Settlement Universal Measures

The Exchange issued Public Notice No. 2268 yesterday morning, stating: "This Exchange is commencing the auction of unified public bonds for spot and futures trading in March and April, as announced in Public Notice No. 2267. Those who have not yet exchanged their old bonds for new ones may use the receipts from the Ministry of Finance Bond Exchange Office or the Central, China, and Communications Banks for settlement. However, the face value of each receipt is limited to 5,000 yuan. The exchange dates are listed below, and this public notice is hereby issued." The exchange dates for old bonds for unified public bonds are as follows: Type A, March 11th; Type B, March 21st; Type C, April 1st; Type D, April 11th; Type E, April 21st.

Public Bonds Printed Exchange Commences

After the issuance of 146 million yuan of unified public bonds on February 1st, the new bonds were printed by the China Book Company and the Commercial Press. It is expected that the printing will be completed by the end of this month, and the bonds will be delivered to the Ministry of Finance. The exchange of old bonds for new bonds must be completed within four months, starting on March 11th, and will be handled by the Bond Exchange Office and the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various locations. The exchange measures have been announced by the Ministry of Finance for public information.

Reconstruction Bonds Issued on the First

Reconstruction Bonds worth 340 million yuan are approved to be issued on March 1st, with an annual interest rate of 6% and a term of 24 years. The purpose is to complete the legal tender policy, strengthen financial organization, support production and construction, balance national treasury revenue and expenditure, and allocate funds for market stabilization. These bonds are also being printed by the China Book Company and the Commercial Press and will soon be completed. As for the date of the auction of Reconstruction Bonds by the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, it is still pending the decision of the Ministry of Finance.

Ministry of Finance Reinstructs Banking and Money Industries to Discuss Reducing Interest Rates Bank Subcommittee to Draft Measures for Associations to Implement

Regarding the issue of reducing interest rates, the Ministry of Finance yesterday reissued instructions to the banking and money industries' trade associations to discuss and submit proposals. At the same time, the Ministry informed the Citizens' Federation. The bank association's subcommittee has drafted opinions and will convene an executive committee meeting in the coming days to discuss them. Details are as follows:

Ministry of Finance Reinstructs

Negotiate and Reduce Interest Rates Yesterday, the banking and money industries' trade associations received an order from the Ministry of Finance stating: "According to the request submitted by the First Special District Citizens' Federation of Shanghai, the petition is to reissue instructions to the Shanghai banking and money industries to reduce loan interest rates and facilitate loan measures in order to promote prosperity. The Shanghai market is declining, and industry and commerce are depressed to an extreme extent. The closure of companies and shops is a daily occurrence. Since the government authorities implemented currency reform measures, the prices of raw materials in various industries have increased, and businesses are suffering from weak purchasing power in the market, leading to further decline. Looking ahead, there are crises everywhere. The association has previously submitted a petition requesting the reissue of instructions to the banking and money industries to reduce loan interest rates, which has been addressed. However, to this day, no implementation has been seen. The association, as a citizens' group, has a deeper understanding and has resolved through regular meetings to resubmit to your ministry, requesting prompt implementation to provide relief and reverse the decline. This matter concerns the relief of Shanghai's commerce and industry, and it is hoped that you will review and handle it accordingly." The order instructs the association to jointly discuss the matter with the money industry association and submit a response. This order is issued.

Inform Citizens' Federation

The First Special District Citizens' Federation of Shanghai received document No. 8707 from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Your petition of February 7, 25th year, requesting the reissue of instructions to the Shanghai banking and money industries to reduce interest rates, has been received and noted. The Shanghai banking and money industries' trade associations have been instructed to jointly discuss and submit a response. You are hereby informed." This approval is issued.

Bank Association

Submits to Executive Committee The Shanghai Banking Industry Association, in accordance with the Ministry's instructions on the issue of reducing interest rates, formed a subcommittee composed of Pan Jiufen of the Bank of China, Zhang Peishen of the Bank of Communications, Ye Fuchi of the Continental Bank, Zhang Naiqi of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhang Jinglu of the Guohua Bank, Zhang Wuyun of the Shanghai Bank, Ji Chang of the Jincheng Bank, Zhang Zhuyu of the Guohuo Bank, and Luo Qinghua of the Silk Industry Bank. The subcommittee convened a meeting on February 10th to discuss the matter. They have now drafted a statement of opinions and submitted it to the Executive Committee for discussion. It is reported that the association will convene an executive committee meeting in the coming days.

Money Industry Association Held Executive Committee Meeting Yesterday Drew Back Hydraulic Construction Bond Collateral

The Shanghai Money Industry Association held its tenth executive committee meeting of the third session at 2 PM yesterday. Currently, the Banking Association is studying methods, and once the methods are determined, they will be discussed and responded to. Reports on the various items of the reserve treasury. (B) Discussion Items: Approval of the letter from the Jiangsu Bank Head Office, which stated that the Jiangsu Finance Department previously mortgaged Hydraulic Construction Bonds to various Shanghai banks and money industries for various loans. The collateral was calculated at 60% of its value. Now that the various loans have been deducted from the principal and interest items in the collateral, and the loans have been reduced, a portion of the collateral should be drawn back to comply with the original 60% plan. They requested the association to hand over the drawn-back bonds for the bank to forward. The discussion resolved to proceed accordingly. Executive Committee Member Chen Lishan resigned for personal reasons. The association intends to reduce expenses by stipulating three patrol police officers for each village alley and dismissing the remaining officers. Charitable and Religious Organizations Gave a Public Farewell Luncheon to Ambassador Xu Over Fifty Celebrities Attended

The Datong News Agency reports that various charitable and religious organizations in the city, recognizing the imminent departure of the newly appointed Ambassador to Japan, Xu Shiying, held a public farewell luncheon at the Jingsu Society on Hart Road yesterday at noon. Over fifty celebrities attended, creating a grand occasion. Details are recorded below:

Celebrities at the Banquet

Representatives of charitable and religious organizations and guests who attended yesterday included Wang Yiting, Zhao Hengti, Zhu Ziqiao, Xiong Bingsan, Zhang Xiaolin, Lu Bohong, Huang Hanzhi, Wu Tiecheng, Mao Yun, Qu Wenliu, Fu Yiting, Li Wuyun, Xu Konglin, Du Yuesheng, Zhu Bianchen, Jin Guanfu, Chen Timin, Qian Jingping, Cheng Jingsheng, Shen Binhan, Feng Yangshan, Zhang Xianqing, Li Jingwei, Pan Renwei, Zai Xianxun, Zhang Lanping, Jiang Baoliu, Quan Shaowu, Weng Yinchu, and Buddhist monks Dabe, Changxing, and Hongming, among over fifty others.

Xiong Xiling's Words

After Mr. Xu arrived at the venue at 12 noon, accompanied by his secretary Huang Bodu, the luncheon began. Xiong Bingsan, the chairman, delivered a speech, stating that Mr. Xu had been handling relief affairs and rescuing disaster victims since 1928, making it his responsibility. Over the years, he has relied on the respect of the disaster victims who were saved. Now that Mr. Xu has been newly appointed by the National Government as the Ambassador to Japan, he should be able to promote understanding between China and Japan and seek peace and happiness for the people, based on his purpose of disaster relief.

Mr. Xu's Response

Next, Mr. Xu delivered a response speech, first stating that from 1931 to August of last year, the total disaster losses in China amounted to 458 million yuan, and the expenses for passive disaster relief amounted to 150 million yuan. Now that the Disaster Relief Committee has been succeeded by Mr. Zhu Ziqiao and others appointed by the government, he is deeply gratified that the right people have been found. He stated firmly that he will make every effort to serve as Ambassador to Japan, upholding the principle of thorough judgment of right and wrong and prioritizing the interests of the country over personal interests. He dares not seek merit but does not expect to be without fault, only hoping to minimize his errors so that he can face himself in the future and also face the friends present. The luncheon ended happily at around 2 PM, and a group photo was taken before dispersing.

New Japanese Ambassador Arida Arrived in Shanghai This Afternoon Horiuchi, Isoya, and Others Came Along

The new Japanese Ambassador to China, Hachiro Arita, departed from Kobe on the Japanese ship Asama Maru the day before yesterday to take up his new post in China. In addition to his wife, those accompanying him to China included Horiuchi, First Secretary of the Embassy, Major General Isoya, Military Attaché, and other staff members. The ship is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 3 PM this afternoon and will dock at the Huishan Wharf. Those arriving to welcome him will include Ambassador Arino of the Japanese Embassy, Consul General Ishiya in Shanghai, Consul General Suma in Beijing, Japanese naval officers stationed in Shanghai, and representatives of Japanese residents. The Chinese municipal authorities will also send representatives to welcome him. After resting briefly in Shanghai, the date of his presentation of credentials in Beijing will depend on the approval of the Chinese government, but it is expected to be around the beginning of next month. It is said that before presenting his credentials in Beijing, Mr. Arida intends to meet with Mr. Xu Shiying, the new Chinese Ambassador to Japan, in Shanghai. (Tokyo Dispatch, 25th, Domei News Agency) The background of Hachiro Arita, the new Japanese Ambassador to China, is as follows: Arita graduated from the Faculty of Law of Tokyo Imperial University in 1909 and then joined the Ministry of Foreign Affairs as Vice Consul in Fengtian. He subsequently served as Consul, Foreign Affairs Official, First Secretary of the Embassy, and Consul General in Chicago, Ottawa, Honolulu, Siam, and other places. While serving as First Secretary of the Embassy in Washington, D.C., he attended the Washington Naval Conference as Secretary-General of the Japanese delegation. He later served as Vice Consul in Tianjin, Minister to Germany, Director of the Asia Bureau, and Ambassador Extraordinary and Plenipotentiary to Hungary. In May 1932, he assumed the position of Foreign Affairs Officer, and in 1933, he was appointed Ambassador to Belgium. He returned to Japan at the end of last year by order of the Foreign Minister and was appointed Ambassador to China on February 7 of this year.

Steamship Industry Association Cables Ministry of Communications: Rescue Ships Trapped by Ice, Send Giant Icebreakers to the Rescue, Airplanes to Transport Fuel and Food

The Shanghai Steamship Industry Association cabled the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating: "Respectfully to the Ministry of Communications, Nanjing: Recently, the climate in the North has been severely cold, and the ice between Tanggu and Dagu has extended for 60 miles, remaining unfrozen for a long time. Ships are trapped within, and fuel and food are running out, creating a perilous situation where the lives of crew and passengers are at risk, unseen in previous years. Although the Tianjin shipping industry has repeatedly attempted icebreaking rescue efforts, they have been ineffective. The Bohai Bay coastline, including the Jieshi River estuary and Qinhuangdao, are similarly icebound, trapping over 30 ships in total. The dangerous situation has been repeatedly reported in newspapers in recent days, urgently requiring rescue. Considering that your Ministry is in charge of maritime administration, we implore you to urgently implement rescue measures for this imminent crisis. This association has repeatedly received requests from member companies to find a way to come forward. Therefore, we respectfully cable you, urging you to promptly consult the Ministry of Finance to instruct the local customs and the Haihe Engineering Bureau to quickly dispatch icebreakers or rent giant foreign icebreakers for immediate rescue. At the same time, order various airline companies to dispatch airplanes to transport fuel and food, so that rescue can be carried out as soon as possible to alleviate the plight of the many ships and avoid further losses. We are extremely anxious and look forward to your response. Respectfully submitted, Yu Hede, Chairman of the Standing Committee of the Shanghai Steamship Industry Association."

The National News Agency reports: "The severe cold in Tianjin, Dagu, and Qinhuangdao has caused the rivers and sea to freeze over, with the ice even thicker than before. Over 30 ships are trapped, and the crews are extremely anxious due to the lack of food and water, sending telegrams to Tianjin and Shanghai to request rescue. Yesterday, reporters continued to interview relevant parties and learned that the Zhongwei Steamship Company's Xin Taiping vessel has been rescued by a Japanese airplane that delivered food supplies. It has been decided that the trapped ships only lack food and water, and coal is mostly sufficient because several ships were originally carrying coal north. The old Taiping ship has now escaped danger. As for the three ships of the Huatong Steamship Company, Zhonghe, Yongxiang, etc., a telegram was received from Tianjin yesterday, stating that the weather there has improved and the area outside the port has cleared up, so the trapped ships are being rescued by Wang Gengsan, President of the Tianjin Shipping Association, who is supervising the Tianxing, a newly constructed iron barge from the Insurance Federation, which is venturing to break the ice." At the same time, the Ministry of Communications has also received a telegram from Hebei Province requesting rescue, so it will dispatch aircraft for assistance within the next few days. The British Taikoo Steamship Company in this city recently had three ships blocked outside Dagu port, and their food is also running out. Yesterday, a large number of workers were dispatched from Shanghai, carrying necessary tools, to travel north by ship for rescue. It was learned yesterday that a total of 34 Chinese and foreign ships were trapped inside and outside Dagu port. This was reported by a telegram from Tianjin, which also stated that the Dagu Pai area outside the port is the shallowest part of the Dagu port entrance, and it has been frozen for a long time with ice piled up like mountains. The trapped ships closer to this area are in extreme danger because once the ice melts, the ice layers may collapse and cause them to sink. Therefore, the relevant steamship companies in Shanghai have sent telegrams to the Tianjin shipping agencies and local authorities, urging them to move the ships as soon as possible to avoid the risk of being submerged when the ice melts."

Dadanshan: Imported Lightship Adrift; Customs Urgently Notifies Companies, Telegrams Reach Merchant Ships En Route

"A Customs lightship originally located at Dadanshan in the Yangtze River estuary, designed to indicate the direction of the waterway and guide ships entering and exiting the Wusongkou from the river and sea, was found to be adrift. The lightship is located 65 nautical miles from Shanghai, between Dadanshan, Niupi, and Jigujiao. Ships arriving in Shanghai from both the North and South Seas and the Yangtze River must rely on the lightship's guidance, making it a true compass for ships entering Shanghai from the river and sea. However, yesterday morning, the Jianghai Customs received a telegram from the French postal ship 'Asia', stating that the Dadanshan import lightship was no longer in its original location, having drifted to a point nine nautical miles east of Dadanshan, specifically at 122 degrees 22 minutes east longitude and 30 degrees 39 minutes north latitude. Upon receiving the report, the Customs recognized the seriousness of the matter, fearing that ships traveling to and from the river and sea, unaware of this incident, would lose guidance and cause a major disaster. Therefore, they immediately notified all shipping companies in the city, instructing them to send telegrams to all ships traveling en route to pay special attention. Meanwhile, Patrol Engineer Carnell dispatched a tugboat to the Dadanshan waters to try to tow the drifting lightship back to its original location to prevent accidents."

Jianghai Customs Takes Over Liebiaozui Lighthouse: Lighthouse Established During the Guangxu Era

"Datong News Agency reports: The Liebiaozui Lighthouse in Dinghai, which was established by civilians, dates back to the 28th year of the Guangxu reign in the late Qing Dynasty, boasting a long and rich history. The expenses for lamp oil and management were all funded by local residents. However, due to the decline of the market, it has become difficult to sustain these expenses, threatening its closure. Upon learning of this situation, Jianghai Customs, recognizing the extreme importance of the lighthouse for navigation, dispatched a patrol engineer yesterday to take it over. In the future, the expenses will be borne by the Customs, and the lighthouse will continue to emit light to benefit shipping."

Two British Airships Still Stranded in Wenzhou; One Remaining in Xiamen Will Not Come to Shanghai

"Of the three British visiting airships, one is repairing its engine in Xiamen, and two departed from Xiamen for Shanghai on the 24th. They encountered fog en route and were forced to land in Wenzhou. Yesterday morning, due to bad weather, they were still stranded in Wenzhou. According to the British aviation attaché, the arrival of these two ships in Shanghai depends on favorable weather conditions. The weather was not good on the 25th, so they did not fly to Shanghai. It is expected that after arriving in Shanghai, they will stay for two days and then fly to Japan for a week-long tour. The one remaining in Xiamen for engine repairs will take more than ten days and will not come to Shanghai. After the two aircraft return from Japan, they will fly to Xiamen or Hong Kong to gather and fly back together."

"Reuters, Shanghai, 25th: Two British airships, which were coming to Shanghai from Xiamen yesterday, were forced to land near Nanguan Harbor, near Wenzhou, en route. According to a telegram received by British naval personnel this afternoon, the British airships were still unable to take off due to poor weather conditions. If the weather improves tomorrow, they can come to Shanghai. A British warship has now arrived in Nanguan from Xiamen to provide assistance. The third airship is still waiting for repairs in Xiamen."

City Telephone Users Insist on Overturning New Fee Regulations; Representatives Appointed to Petition Municipal Council Today; Letter to Chinese Directors Requesting Public Negotiation to Console Public Hope

"Shen Shi News Agency reports: The Shanghai Telephone Company's implementation of new fee regulations is imminent. In order to thoroughly resist and find effective ways to deal with this, various sectors of the city have requested the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concessions to convene a ratepayers' meeting to gather the strength of all city users as a backing. They have sent a letter to the Chinese directors attending the Municipal Council regarding the compromise measures proposed, which citizens in various districts have expressed their opposition to. Details are as follows:"

"New Fee Regulations Must Be Overturned"

"The Special District Telephone Issue Committee, in order to convey the intentions of various groups and negotiate with the Municipal Council regarding the Telephone Company's changes to fee regulations, has specifically appointed Qu Zhenhua, Mao Yun, Li Biekuai, Zhang Yiying, Gong Jingyan, Ke Ganchen, Gu Wensheng, and seven others to petition the Chairman of the Municipal Council, Mr. Fessenden, this afternoon at 3:00 PM. They will demand that the Telephone Company's new fee regulations be fundamentally overturned. At the very least, the basic number of calls must be calculated at three cents per call in order to be fair; otherwise, they will not hesitate to make any sacrifice."

"Meeting Tomorrow to Report Progress"

"The committee has also scheduled to hold its third Board of Directors meeting yesterday to report on the progress of the petition to the concession authorities. A notice has already been issued, stating: 'Regarding the imminent implementation of the new telephone system, if we do not actively proceed, it will definitely cause delay. Therefore, on the 26th of this month, Qu Zhenhua and seven others will be appointed to petition the Municipal Council to negotiate the cancellation of the price increase. A third Board of Directors meeting will be held on the 27th to report on the progress. This matter is of great importance, please do not ignore it.'"

"Letter Requesting Chinese Directors to Conduct Public Negotiations"

"The 12th, 15th, 36th, 38th, and 39th district branches of the First Special District Citizens' Union of this city have expressed dissatisfaction with the measures proposed by the Chinese directors. Yesterday, they specifically jointly sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concessions, requesting that the basic number of calls be uniformly calculated at three cents per call and requesting continued resistance. The original letter reads: 'The Shanghai Telephone Company, in order to satisfy its desire for an annual interest of one percent, has specifically promulgated new regulations that charge by call. City users absolutely cannot agree to this kind of disguised price increase. We have requested your association's directors attending the Municipal Council to strongly resist. If it is necessary to calculate by call, the basic number of calls must also be calculated at a rate of three cents, that is, a business telephone with a monthly fee of ten yuan should have 333 calls, and a residential telephone with a monthly fee of six yuan and five jiao should have 216 calls, in order to be fair. Otherwise, the charge of three cents per call for exceeding the basic number of calls is more than double the cost of 6.6 cents per call for the basic calls. The unreasonableness of this measure is very obvious. Therefore, we have repeatedly requested your association to convene a ratepayers' meeting to solicit the opinions of all users in order to collectively resist. However, according to the newspapers, your association held its sixth executive committee meeting on the 22nd and surprisingly agreed with the directors' opinions, changing the basic calls for business telephones to 200 and residential telephones to 150. If the company's net profit exceeds 10 percent, prices should be immediately reduced, and the more calls used, the lower the cost per call, etc. It seems that this kind of opinion is absolutely a minority opinion, and it is unlikely that all taxpayers in the city will agree. Therefore, we specifically jointly send a letter to your association to convey to the directors attending the Municipal Council that the city's users absolutely cannot agree unless the basic calls are based on a standard of three cents. We believe that all the directors have a heavy responsibility entrusted to them by the taxpayers of the city and will definitely uphold public opinion and work hard to negotiate in order to console public hope.'"

Finance Ministry Improves Methods for Customs Inspection of Overseas Chinese Entering and Leaving the Country; Instructs Director General of Customs to Draft Six Measures

"Shen Shi News Agency reports: According to news from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, overseas Chinese organizations and returned overseas Chinese often complain that the customs in various ports of South China often make things difficult when inspecting the luggage of overseas Chinese entering and leaving the country, or even harass them. They have repeatedly complained to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has successively sent letters to the Ministry of Finance, requesting that they find ways to eliminate this. The Ministry of Finance, together with the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, dispatched personnel to various ports in South China to conduct on-site investigations. They found that the various complaints made by overseas Chinese, due to different environmental conditions in each port, resulted in various difficulties and misunderstandings, and that such incidents sometimes occurred. They ordered the Director General of Customs to draft six measures for improvement, seeking the consent of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission considered the measures to be fair and fully agreed. They will be implemented separately by the Ministry of Finance. The measures are as follows: It is proposed that the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission find a way to have the consulates of our country abroad, chambers of commerce of our country, or overseas Chinese associations, etc., be responsible for issuing (A) a certificate to each overseas Chinese person when they return to their country. This certificate must have a photograph of the person attached, and a detailed list of the personal and household items they are carrying, as well as miscellaneous items. The validity of this certificate is limited to one trip. (B) A booklet explaining the various rules and regulations of Chinese Customs for managing passenger luggage. This booklet should be compiled by the Customs and printed and distributed by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. It is proposed that the government issue a circular to local authorities, assisting the Customs in prohibiting smugglers from boarding ships as soon as they arrive in port. It is proposed to negotiate with the Xinning Railway Bureau to expand and improve the Beijie wharf on that road. If this cannot be done, the Customs will find ways to build appropriate wharves and inspection facilities for use. It is proposed that the Director General of Customs issue a circular to all ports, instructing all foreign customs officers to treat passengers on ships with courtesy. If passengers refuse to follow customs procedures, they must also maintain a peaceful attitude to persuade them to comply and must not be rude. If they do not comply, their promotion will be suspended as a warning. It is proposed that the Jianghai Customs dispatch customs officers to board incoming ships passing through Hengmen, to strictly search all parts of the ship, except for passenger cabins and passenger luggage, on the way from the incoming ship to Jiangmen, and to prevent private goods from being thrown into the sea along the way. Passenger cabins will be searched after the passengers disembark at Beijie, and passenger luggage will be inspected uniformly at the wharf to avoid the trouble of mixing and duplication, and the practice of hiding private goods can also be prevented in advance. However, if this is done, although the customs will increase the number of investigators, the Customs Commissioner of the port can propose the number of additional personnel that should be increased and submit it for approval. The Qionghai Customs' current method of inspecting passenger luggage on board ships is proposed to be discontinued, as the luggage will be transported by barges at that time, and this kind of inspection cannot be handled perfectly in a short period of time."

"After the National Gold and Silver Shop Industry Federation decided to organize a petitioning group, representatives from various provinces and cities have been appointed and reported to the Shanghai Gold and Silver Shop Industry Association. Representatives from Nanjing City, including Ran Xizhang, took the Shanghai-Pinglian Yun through train back to Beijing at 4:05 PM yesterday to prepare for the reception of petitioning representatives from the national industry, and to arrange everything. They are scheduled to assemble at the Beijing Gold and Silver Shop Industry Association this morning and petition the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance from 9:00 AM."

"Dinner Last Night"

"Fourteen representatives from the old generation of Shanghai industry, including Ying Xiansan, Qi Heqing, Xu Weicai, Zhu Tingxiang, Cai Pinde, Song Songling, Qian Qitang, Zhou Gengchu, Feng Changmiao, Hu Picheng, Feng Qingan, Ge Junqing, and Yao Yuhao, thirteen representatives from the new generation, including Sun Yonglin, Chen Dexin, and Dong Xuepeng, as well as representatives from provinces such as Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Hebei, Shandong, Fujian, Sichuan, and cities such as Hankou, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, and Nanchang, including Gu Sumin, Yu Shanfu, and Zou Hexuan, gathered at the association's meeting room in Nanjing Huayuan Lane at 5:00 PM yesterday to prepare for the petitioning trip to Beijing, and had dinner at the association at 7:00 PM."

"Assembled at North Station"

"A total of more than 50 representatives from various provinces and cities assembled at the Shanghai North Station at 10:00 PM yesterday, led by Ying Zisan (Standing Committee Member of the Shanghai Gold and Silver Shop Industry Association), carrying the petition. They took the Beijing-Shanghai night express train at 11:00 PM to Beijing. Representatives from Shanghai Laofengxiang, Qingfuxing, and Yang Qinghe, both old and new, as well as workers, went to the North Station to see them off. After arriving in Beijing this morning, they will immediately jointly petition, demanding the amendment of the Silver Product Silver Usage Management Regulations. The objectives are: Jewelry silver should still use pure silver. Utensils and gifts can use 80% silver. Furthermore, Fu Shengmao, Chairman of the Shanghai Gold and Silver Shop Industry Association, canceled his trip to Beijing due to his unhealed foot injury."

"Another Telegram of Appeal"

"The association telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: 'We have found that our gold and silver shop industry has, since November of last year, received the Silver Usage Management Regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Finance, limiting the use of chemical silver to manufacture utensils and ornaments, and only allowing a maximum of 30% pure silver to be added when necessary. Merchants and the public know that chemical silver is rigid and fragile, making it difficult to manufacture by hand, which will cause hundreds of thousands of workers in the national industry to be unemployed. We have submitted another request to amend the regulations to exempt the restrictions, but it has not been approved. On the 23rd of this month, more than 600 representatives gathered in Shanghai to hold a joint meeting of the national gold and silver shop industry, borrowing the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Together we decided to send representatives to Beijing to petition and earnestly appeal to the authorities. We respectfully request your inspection and implore you to show compassion, so as to achieve the purpose of amending the regulations and exempting the restrictions in order to maintain the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of people in the national industry. We are very anxious and implore you to grant our prayer.'"

Datong Xing Steamship Company Refuses the Tongshun Crew's Request for Relief; Crew Members Submit Separate Petitions to the Maritime Administration Bureau and the Seamen's Union, Requesting Serious Negotiations with the Company

"The Tongshun ship of the Datong Xing Steamship Company in this city ran aground near Mafu Cape on Hainan Island on the 8th of this month due to fog. All 64 crew members, except for the captain, Pu Li, who remained in Hong Kong to negotiate with the insurance company, arrived in Shanghai on the 20th and 24th of this month. They are temporarily staying in hotels and are in a dire situation. The crew members, having survived the grounding, suffered losses as their luggage was sacrificed. They requested compensation for their losses and relief from the company yesterday. However, the company not only refused to provide relief and compensation, but also indicated that it would dismiss all crew members. The crew members, finding that their requests were not being met, drafted petitions and submitted them to the Maritime Administration Bureau and the Seamen's Union yesterday morning, requesting serious negotiations with the company in order to achieve the goal of obtaining compensation and relief."

Dr. Wang Guangqi Passed Away in Germany

Dr. Wang Guangqi went to Germany to study in the ninth year of the Republic of China (1920). For sixteen years, he initially studied political economy, and for the past ten years, he specialized in music. In the twenty-third year of the Republic of China (1934), he obtained a doctoral degree from the University of Bonn. His dissertation was titled "The Ancient Chinese Opera." He had a wealth of writings throughout his life, with more than forty kinds published domestically. His contribution to the academic and ideological circles of our country was rarely seen in recent times. His strict self-discipline and diligence in learning were sufficient to be a model for others. Unfortunately, he recently suffered from cerebral congestion and passed away in Bonn, on the banks of the Rhine River in Germany. He died young while diligently pursuing his studies, fulfilling his ambitions until the end, which is truly a great loss to the nation's talent. It is said that his old friends, Mr. Shu Xincheng of the Compilation and Translation Institute of the Zhonghua Book Company, Mr. Zuo Shunsheng of the Central Political School, and Mr. Wei Shizhen of the National Sichuan University, etc., plan to compile a general catalog of Mr. Wang's posthumous works in the near future, and publish a special commemorative volume to express their condolences. It is noted that Mr. Wang once served as a correspondent for this newspaper in Germany.

Mr. Shengjia Lectures on the Development of Internal Combustion Engines

Yesterday afternoon, the Chinese Institute of Engineers held a gathering, where the famous engineer Mr. Shengjia lectured on the development of internal combustion engines. In essence, the progress of aircraft engines and automobile engines is advancing by leaps and bounds, almost exceeding expectations. However, the development of diesel engines has reached a point where further major progress is unlikely. Ultra-high-pressure internal combustion engines are a new invention, and the future development and progress of this is unlimited. Mr. Shengjia also pointed out the path of improvement and progress, but the nature is extremely specialized, so it is not recorded.
