Yangshupu Road, Weixing Lane: Fire Claims Four Lives, Child Thrown from Window, Three Houses Destroyed, Two Children Injured

The houses on No. 152, Yangshupu Road (i.e., Weixing Lane), are all one-story above another, commonly known as "Japanese houses." At around 10:30 yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the home of Yang Xiaorong at No. 12 in the lane. The stairs were also burned, and the tenants of the Tang and Wu families living upstairs, finding their escape route cut off, hurriedly threw their children from the window. Fortunately, neighbors on the left and right heard the alarm and gathered together, and cooperated in catching them below the window. However, the fire was extremely fierce at the time, with thick smoke and flames reaching the sky. Therefore, in a short while, the house had turned to ashes. The house was crowded with people, and some were unable to escape. In addition, the two buildings to the left and right, Nos. 10 and 14, were also on fire, causing the neighbors to be too busy fleeing for their lives to continue rescuing people, leaving the fire to spread. For a time, the noise was deafening, and the order was chaotic. The cries shook heaven and earth. The nearby yamen (police) received the news and immediately telegraphed the Central Fire Brigade, which informed the Yangshupu Fire Brigade to rush fire trucks and ambulances to put out the fire. They vigorously sprayed water while rescuing people. They rescued two children from the fire pit, one named Tang Rongzhang, twelve years old, and the other named Tang Baogen, only three years old. However, both were burned all over their bodies and were rushed to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment, in critical condition. The fire was completely extinguished at around 12:00. As a result, three houses, Nos. 10, 12, and 14, were burned down, and all the property was destroyed. Afterwards, firefighters dug through the fire site and found a middle-aged woman and three children buried in the fire pit, with charred heads and faces, and a foul odor, the scene was unbearable to witness. After being identified by the neighbors, it was learned that the woman was Wu Kongshi, a Ningbo woman residing in the front building of No. 12, forty years old, who had just moved in last week. Now she encounters this disaster, is this her fate? Among the three children, two were Wu Kongshi's sons, the elder named Wu Xiaomao, seven years old, and the younger named Wu Xiaogen, four years old. There was also a son of the Tang family, named Tang Mingfang, nine years old. At the time, once their deaths were confirmed, their family members cried to the heavens and earth, wailing uncontrollably. Those who saw it could not help but feel grief. The firefighters and detectives consoled them, and then sent the four corpses to the coroner's office to be examined, and after the examination, they would be coffined and buried. An investigation into the cause of the fire will be conducted to bring those responsible to justice.

Since the beginning of spring, the weather has not yet warmed up, and there has been a lot of rain. Yesterday morning, rain and snow fell again, ceasing not all day, and the weather was even colder. This kind of abnormal weather is rare in recent years.

Tracks Slippery, Tram Derailed, Damaging a Rickshaw, Passengers and Rickshaw Puller Fortunately Unharmed

The tram of the French Tram Company running on the Sixteenth Puli Road, driven by driver No. 74, departed from the Lujiazui factory at 8:50 yesterday morning. When it drove to the junction of Fangxie Road and Wansheng Bridge in the South City, due to the rain and snow, the tracks were slippery, causing all four wheels of the tram to derail. A rickshaw carrying passengers from north to south failed to avoid it, and the wheels were completely damaged. Fortunately, the passengers were unharmed. The police and company ticket inspectors arrived, recorded the numbers of the driver and rickshaw, and dragged the derailed wheels back onto the track, restoring traffic. The damaged rickshaw was taken by the rickshaw puller Chen Jinsheng to the Ximen Branch for investigation and compensation.

Temples in This City Will Be Re-registered Next Month, Set from March 2nd to the End of June

According to Guomin News, regarding the issue of temple registration in this port, the municipal government has already undertaken it. In May of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China (1929), all 103 case files were ordered to be handled by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The bureau accepted and started registering temples, and to date, 4 case files have been approved, and 252 have not been approved. However, the Ministry of the Interior has stipulated that the temple registration case should be handled by the Social Affairs Bureau of each province and city, and the municipal government has been consulted to instruct the affiliated departments to comply. It is now known that after Bureau Chief Wu Xingya was ordered, he instructed Sun Yongyi, director of the fourth section of the Public Welfare Department, to handle the matter and report back. Director Sun took the document to the Public Security Bureau at 2:00 yesterday afternoon to accept all the case files. Hong Qi, chief of the second section of the Public Security Bureau, dispatched staff member Jin Zhongjian to handle the transfer. According to Sun, the registration of temples in this city will begin on March 2nd (next Monday) and will end at the end of June this year. Regardless of whether they have been registered or have requested registration but have not been approved, they will all be re-registered.

Special Second Court Investigates Yesterday, Gu Zhuxuan's Family Denies Bribery, Gu Songmao Pays 1,000 Yuan Bail

Gu Zhuxuan, the main criminal who instigated the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, was sentenced to fifteen years in prison by the Special Second Court and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. After the trial, a case of bribery and retraction of testimony and escape from prison by a guard was discovered. The Special Second Prosecutor's Office has been conducting a strict investigation for more than half a month. The details have been recorded in previous reports. At 9:30 yesterday morning, Prosecutor Wang Ren arrived at the Sixth Investigation Office to question Gu Zhuxuan's three elder brothers, Gu Songmao, and Gu's family members, Gu Cai, Gu Li, Gu's brother-in-law Zheng Jian, and the director of the detention center, Wu, and guard Ma Xinchang, and six other people. Because the prosecutor ordered outsiders not to be allowed to listen, the details could not be recorded. According to reporters, the content of the investigation was to investigate the 3,000 yuan deposit in the name of Zhang Sen, a client of the Daya Bank, and whether there was bribery of the guards to buy the retraction of the prisoner's testimony. Gu's family members all vehemently denied everything. As a result, the prosecutor ordered the two guards, Wu and Ma, not to leave their posts during the investigation period. Gu Songmao paid a cash bond of 1,000 yuan to be available for summons at any time, otherwise he would be taken into custody. The court adjourned at 11:00 noon.

Famous Hunter Initiates Wildlife Refuge for Wild Birds

According to the Great America Evening News, Mr. Keming, a well-known broker and hunter in this port, and Mr. Wilkinson, a well-known ornithologist and author of books on birds, in order to preserve the lives of many birds that pass through Shanghai every year, intend to strive to designate the western and northeastern areas of Shanghai as wildlife refuges, where hunting is not allowed. The two men will ask Mayor Wu to approve the addition of Greater Shanghai to the plan, and request the central authorities to cooperate in its implementation within their jurisdiction. The Shanghai Western Bird Sanctuary will be bounded by the Suzhou River and Bubbling Well Road, and will extend south from the airfield to the Huangpu River, with an area of at least twenty square miles. According to Mr. Keming, this move does not hinder legal hunters, because if they want to hunt birds, they can go to a slightly farther place. Many birds with beautiful voices and feathers fly from outside to Shanghai every year, looking very tired. Hunters shoot birds at sight, without any distinction, and the orioles that fly in summer are especially admired by them. The reason why they want to protect the birds around Shanghai is to keep them for the enjoyment of the residents, and because Shanghai is densely populated, hunting here can easily injure or kill people with stray bullets. This has been seen many times in the past. The initiators hope that the Chinese and foreign authorities and residents will cooperate with this plan.

Insurance Customer, American Woman Commits Suicide by Shooting

Ms. Woen, an American woman who worked in the insurance business and was thirty-seven years old, committed suicide by shooting herself at around 9:15 yesterday morning at her residence at No. 760, HSBC Building. She was shot in the head. The servant heard the sound and went to check, and Ms. Woen was lying in a pool of blood, with a pistol next to her. She was rushed to the Public Hospital for treatment, but died of her injuries in the afternoon. Ms. Woen was not married, her family was in the United States, and she had been in Shanghai for about five years. The insurance management office where she worked had recently closed. Her suicide was probably due to financial difficulties. When the American authorities examined the body yesterday, no suicide note was found.

Moving Due to Rumors, Maid Steals Items, Case of Ding Peng's Death from Anger Solved, Maid Apprehended in Huzhou

In November of last year, due to rumors in Zhabei, the general public was like frightened birds, and moved to the concession one after another. Peng, the wife of Ding Bingchang, a Wuxi native at No. 316, Zhonghua Xin Road, also temporarily hid her valuable suitcases and items in the concession. Unexpectedly, the maid Wang seized the opportunity to steal a valuable clothes box and fled without a trace. The box contained diamond rings, pearls, gold jewelry, jade, gemstones, etc., worth more than 3,000 yuan. Although the matter was reported to the Yongxing Road Police Station for investigation, no progress had been made to this day. The mistress Ding Peng died of grief and anger because of this. It is now known that after several months, the case was recently solved by the Detective Brigade of the Huzhou Security Command in Zhejiang Province at No. 3, Shijia Lane, in the city. After the team confirmed the facts, they notified the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to come and escort the suspect back to Shanghai. The Detective Brigade of the North Station Branch also summoned Ding Bingchang, the owner of the stolen goods, to identify the stolen items. The maid confessed that her real name was Peng Ge, forty-two years old, from Danyang, and that she falsely claimed to be Wang. In November of last year, she was introduced by Lu, a barber at the intersection of Henan Road and Aeherjin Road in North Shanghai, to work as a maid in the Ding family. When the Ding family was moving, she saw a leather handbag and a tin box containing a lot of jewelry. She stole them when the owner was unprepared. She stayed in a hotel that night, and the next morning, she pawned three strings of large and small pearls at a pawnshop in Huangpu for 80 yuan to use as travel expenses. She took a boat to Huzhou to her lover Zhao Honggen. All the gold jewelry was sold to gold shops for more than 400 yuan. Only three large pearls and a gold bracelet were given to Zhou Xia, the woman she lived with. The rest was cheated away by her lover. After reviewing the confession, Gu Liancheng and Guo Mengqu, the deputy chiefs of the team, dispatched detectives Zhang Dalong and Jiao Bingyun to retrieve the original pawn tickets.

Robbers Burglarize and Murder on Gordon Road, Owner Subdues One Robber, Lu San is Tragically Killed by Robber's Gunshot Wound to Vital Spot, Owner Bites Robber's Wrist to Capture Him

The home of Lu Shide, a Jiangbei native at No. 584, Yodah Corner, Gordon Road in Western Shanghai, was suddenly broken into by two robbers, Li Yisan and Dakezi, both from Jiangbei, at 6:30 the day before yesterday afternoon. Dakezi held the door, and Li took out a pistol in the living room, threatening Lu Shide, his wife Lu Wang, and his son Lu Xuewu not to shout. He forced Lu Wang to remove the gold earrings she was wearing. At that time, Lu Shide's brother, Lu San, also known as Zhao Fuhai (49 years old, from Jiangbei), heard the alarm in the back room and walked out of the room. The robber Li immediately fired a shot at him.

The bullet hit his forehead, and at that time, the robber holding the door saw that he had already caused a disaster, and fled on foot. Li Yisan, who fired the gun, also tried to turn around and escape, but Lu Xuewu stepped forward and grabbed Li's right hand holding the gun. Li was in a hurry and fired several more shots, all of which missed. However, because Li was tall and strong, and Lu Xuewu was determined to resist, they twisted together into a ball, and gradually twisted out of the door. The injured Lu San and Lu Wang also chased out of the door, but because Lu San's injuries were too severe and he lacked the strength to support himself, he fell to the ground at the door of his residence, blood gushing out like a spring.

He fainted immediately. At that time, Lu Xuewu and Lu Wang had grabbed the robber Li's left and right hands, and Lu Xuewu bit down hard on the robber Li's right wrist, causing Li to be in pain and drop the pistol. Someone was sent to report to the No. 22 Indian police to arrest Li and seize a pistol, which had no bullets in it. The Indian police telegraphed the Gordon Road Police Station, which immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate, and found a shell casing and a bullet, and then Li was taken into custody at the police station. The injured Lu San was sent to the St. Luke's Hospital, but because the injury was to the brain,

He died shortly after, and the body was sent to the Pei Lun Road coroner's office for examination. Yesterday morning, the police sent Li Yisan to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin prosecuted him for robbery and murder according to Article 332, Paragraph 4 of the Criminal Code, and stated the above situation, saying that according to the defendant's confession in the police station, he did not know Dakezi, who was at large, and was introduced by Mei Shitian. The police, together with the Public Security Bureau, went to No. 15, Qia Jian Fruit, Tanziwan Road, Zhabei, and arrested Mei, who is now detained by the Public Security Bureau, and requested that the court prepare a document to transfer him

To the court for investigation, etc. Subsequently, Lu Wang and Lu Xuewu filed a case to prove everything, and Lu Xuewu confessed that he was injured in his thumb when he grabbed the defendant's hand holding the gun and the defendant resisted by firing the gun, etc. In response, the defendant Li Yisan confessed to going with Dakezi to rob, but denied deliberately firing the gun and killing Lu San, saying that it was because his hand holding the gun was grabbed by Lu Xuewu and the pistol was snatched away, causing him to accidentally touch the trigger, and the bullet was shot out and hit the deceased, etc. Judge Wu Zehan reviewed the confession and considered that it was necessary to

Inspect the scene of the incident, and ordered the defendant to be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing for the morning of March 3, and scheduled to go to the site for inspection at 2:00 pm on March 2. After the ruling, the defendant was taken down by the detective and transferred to the coroner's office. Prosecutor Zhang Zongru arrived at the office and examined the body, and then ruled that the deceased Lu San, male, died of a gunshot wound before death, and the body was handed over to his family Lu Xuewu to claim and bury. The murderer Li Yisan and the pistol were sent to the court by the police for handling.

Luodian Town: Gambling Collapse Tragedy, More Than Ten People Bleeding, Seriously and Minorly Injured

At around 10:00 the day before yesterday evening, the Gong Rende cigarette paper and sundries store, household No. 9, 15th Jia, 1st Bao, South Lane Street, Luodian Town, Baoshan County, through which the Shanghai-Taicang long-distance bus passes, gathered seventy or eighty gamblers. They were gambling on pai gow on the mezzanine floor behind the store. It was known that there were too many people and the mezzanine floor was not strong enough. With a crash, the mezzanine floor collapsed, resulting in a tragic incident of broken arms, broken feet, and bloody heads. The director of the Public Security Third Branch in the town, Director Dong, learned of this and sent the police to summon the store owner Gong Qingxiang, who had already fled. Only Gong's father, named A Da, and a cohabitant, Zhu Afu, were brought to the case. Director Dong then found that there were more than ten people who were slightly and seriously injured. Those with more serious injuries included Zheng Zongheng, who was injured in the head, forehead, and left hand dislocated; Cai A'er, who had a broken foot bone; Zhang Amao, who was injured in the ankle; Yang Maoquan, whose hands and feet were dislocated, etc. Those with minor injuries were all sent to the hospital for treatment. It is still impossible to predict whether there is any danger to life. However, the case involves gathering people to gamble, so it was sent to the county government yesterday afternoon for interrogation.

Ignoring Mortgage Payments, Sheng Yuchang is Accused

Sheng Yuchang, the eldest grandson of Sheng Xingxun, a courtier of the late Qing Dynasty, mortgaged 14 mu of cemetery land at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Baker Road to the China Business Company on March 7, 1933, for 650,000 taels of silver, totaling 909,090.91 yuan in national currency, with an agreed interest rate of 9% per annum. When it was due on March 1 of last year, China Business Company repeatedly urged him to redeem it, but Sheng ignored it. The company then hired lawyer Yang Ruinian to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, demanding the return of 987,000 yuan in national currency. Yesterday morning, Judge Li of the Sixth Civil Court summoned him. The defendant Sheng Yuchang hired a lawyer to present a defense, stating that the defendant previously had 16,000 shares of the Sanxin Yarn Factory's stock, and had mortgaged it to the China Business Company for 400,000 taels of silver. Later, Sanxin was sold to others by the company in 1931 for 4.5 million taels, leaving 4.3 million taels after deducting the commission of 200,000. The defendant should have received one-fifth, which is 860,000 taels. The plaintiff has not yet paid this amount to the defendant and should be used to offset the mortgage. Plaintiff Yang Ruinian, on the other hand, stated that all the funds of Sanxin had been cleared. Judge Li considered that it was necessary to investigate the case and ordered it to be rescheduled for questioning.

The Two Roads Administration Stipulates Measures for Selling Old Railroad Ties

The Roads Administration believes that there are no explicit regulations for employees of the Roads Administration and the troops stationed along the line to purchase old railroad ties. It has formulated eight provisional measures, which were submitted to the 65th Roads Administration meeting for approval. In addition to submitting them to the ministry for record, the Roads Administration has issued orders to all departments to comply. The original text is as follows: 1. Old railroad ties are divided into hardwood and American pine. Hardwood sells for 40 cents of national currency per tie, and American pine sells for 20 cents of national currency per tie. This is limited to track ties. Bridge and switch ties are not sold. 2. Employees of this Roads Administration may purchase old railroad ties at a rate of up to 2 yuan of national currency per person per month. Amounts above 2 yuan must be approved in writing by the relevant departments. 3. Troops stationed along this Roads Administration who are responsible for protecting the roads or trains may also purchase old railroad ties, but must be certified in writing by the relevant officer. 4. For all purchases of old railroad ties, the price must first be paid to the general affairs section of the engineering department nearby, or to the engineering sections along the line. 5. After receiving the payment for the old railroad ties, the general affairs section of the engineering department or the various engineering sections should immediately issue a receipt and a pickup certificate. 6. All old railroad ties picked up with a pickup certificate are the responsibility of the purchaser. This Roads Administration will not provide delivery. 7. All proceeds from the sale of old railroad ties shall be remitted to the accounting department by the engineering department at any time. 8. If the number of old railroad ties is not large and must be reserved for use in engineering, each engineering section may temporarily suspend issuing them.

Public Concession: Overview of Last Year's Public Works Report

According to the 1935 work report of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, the completed construction projects that year included the following: One bridge project, consisting of two reinforced concrete bridges at Pingji and Dinghai Roads, each sixty in length; in terms of buildings, there were the Central Police Station on Fuzhou Road, the Chengdu Road Police Station and housing, the Huade Road West Prison, the expanded part of the Public Works Bureau meat market and slaughterhouse on Qinqin Road, the abandoned animal disposal station on Qinqin Road, the expansion of the Tongzhou Road vegetable market, the reconstruction of the Huishan public pier, the central laundry of the Public Works Bureau Hospital on Feilun Road, and the Zhoushan Road hygiene branch, etc.; In terms of roads, important sections of Nanjing Road, Henan Road, Broadway Road, Beijing Road, Avenue Edward VII, etc., were widened, with a total of more than 14,000 cubic yards of roadbed and pavement construction; about half a mile of pavement was rebuilt with concrete and asphalt. All the streetlights within the concession have now been converted to electric lights. The revetment constructed on Dixiwei Road is approximately one hundred yards in length. In addition to the Huishan public pier, the floating pier on the Bund of Beijing Road has also been renovated. A total of six and a quarter miles of drains and sewage pipes were laid. In terms of parks, the construction of the Huzhou Road Park was completed in that year. A new stone crushing machine was installed at the Pingqiao Stone Quarry. Due to financial constraints, the larger of the above public buildings were limited to those that had already commenced construction in the previous year.

Regarding private construction, projects this year were even more reduced compared to the previous year. The total value of new buildings was just over ten million, whereas in 1934 it was still over twenty-seven million six hundred and sixty thousand. The total population surveyed within the concession this year was approximately 1.15 million, an increase of 150,000 people compared to five years ago. However, during these years, there has been no excessive construction of housing, and there are still crowded conditions in the residences of poor residents within the concession. It is expected that when economic conditions recover in the future, new construction will commence.

Regarding private construction, although the number of buildings has decreased, violations of construction regulations are almost innumerable. This may be related to the social economy. On the one hand, builders are trying to save as much as possible, and on the other hand, contractors are also trying to cut corners and reduce materials to compete with each other. Furthermore, there is another matter that should be noted regarding wooden buildings within the concession, namely, the gradual spread of termites, which is a major concern for the future. Therefore, when constructing, if one is concerned that the wood contains these pests and wants to eliminate them, one can contact the Public Works Department for instructions on how to eliminate them.

Regarding the staff of the Public Works Department, the head of the department took leave to return to his country on July 1 and did not return until November 19. During this period, the extra head of the department acted as head of affairs. Ten new employees were hired this year, one died, eleven resigned, and three were transferred to other locations. The total number of foreign employees this year was 120, a decrease of five from the previous year. The number of Chinese employees has also decreased from 539 last year to 534 this year.

Lawsuit over HSBC Shares after Liu Zanqi's Death: Liu's Wife Sues Her Aunt to Transfer the Shares; Family Members Also Join the Lawsuit

Liu Weichuan, a wealthy merchant from Guangdong, and his wife, Tian Xiangyun, had two sons and two daughters together. The eldest son was named Zanlin, who married Qian Suyu. The second son was Zanqi, who married Guo Xiurong. The eldest daughter was Huiyan, and the second daughter was Minyan. In the nineteenth year, Liu Weichuan went bankrupt due to business failure and soon passed away. Zanlin also died of illness without any heirs. Zanqi had three sons and one daughter: Rongzu, Yaozu, Guangzu, and the youngest daughter, Guoying. Guangzu was then adopted as Zanlin's heir. Zanqi served as the manager of the Yongtaihe Yinxing Company's Beijing branch. Last October, he also died in Tianjin due to a sudden cerebral hemorrhage. Now, Liu Guo Xiurong suddenly, along with her sons Rongzu and Yaozu, and daughter Guoying, hired a lawyer to sue her aunt Tian Xiangyun in the First Special District Court, requesting confirmation of inheritance rights. The subject of the lawsuit is ten shares of HSBC bank stock, with a market value of tens of thousands of dollars. The reason is that the shares were used as a guarantee for Zanqi's employment. Now, the aunt has taken the shares and transferred them. Therefore, they request confirmation of the inheritance rights to the shares. Liu Tian Xiangyunyun also hired lawyer Zhang Ziyun to defend, stating that the HSBC shares have always belonged to the defendant. Because Zanqi joined Yongtaihe, she deposited them into the company as collateral. Later, when he was promoted to manager, he requested to transfer the account to his name for the sake of appearances. When Zanqi died, she took them back and entrusted a lawyer to correct the account name, as evidenced by Zanqi's letters. Liu Qian Suyu, Liu Huiyan, and Liu Minyan believed that they all had a relationship with these rights and could not allow Guo Xiurong to take possession of them alone. Therefore, they also hired lawyer Yang Guoshu to join the lawsuit. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Mo Runhua opened the sixth civil court to summon them. After the lawyers for the plaintiff, defendant, and intervenors presented their reasons, the court ordered a postponement for another hearing.

In addition, the patriotic enthusiasm of overseas Chinese and the psychology of using national products happily are well known to the Chinese people. In recent years, the progress of the motherland's national product industries, as well as the excellence of the products, and their degree, may not be fully known to overseas Chinese. The Owner of the Barge Sunk by the New Jiangtian Wheel Reports to the Navigation Bureau: Only Eight of the Eleven Crew Members Survived; The Navigation Bureau Will Summon the Captain of the Jiangtian Wheel for Questioning

According to the Central News Agency, the New Jiangtian Wheel of the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company recently collided with and sank a large barge while entering Shanghai from Ningbo. Because the wheel's rescue was ineffective, it immediately sailed to Shanghai and reported to the Navigation Administration and the Port Affairs Bureau. At that time, it was only known that the barge had sunk, and all the crew members were missing. It is now learned that nine of the crew members were fortunate enough to jump into a sampan and drift to Pudong, where they were rescued. They then reported the incident to the Navigation Administration a few days ago. The details are as follows:

The Barge Owner Reports to the Navigation Bureau:

After the incident of the New Jiangtian Wheel colliding with the barge occurred, the wheel's captain, Qiang Sheng, and first mate, Yu Tingyuan, and others, submitted reports to the Navigation Administration and the Port Affairs Bureau. However, at that time, because the barge sank and the crew members were missing, it was not possible to determine who was responsible. The Navigation Administration then sent letters to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Jianghai Customs to inquire about the details, but no reply was received. Several days ago, news of the rescue was reported, but no one came to the bureau to report. It was not until last Saturday that a person named Luo Xingchun, claiming to be the owner of the barge, and his helmsman, Chen Tianqing, came to the bureau to identify and report the incident. The bureau then took a written statement from him.

The Barge Was Carrying Oil to Ningbo on the Day of the Collision:

According to Luo's statement, he is the owner of the barge, 55 years old, from Huangyan. The barge's name is Jin Wanli, it cost 14,000 yuan to build, and has a capacity of 1,200 bags of rice. It is registered with the Haimen Navigation Administration and is used to transport cargo. On this occasion, it was chartered to load 360 barrels of Texaco diesel oil, weighing 60 tons, in Shanghai and was sailing to Ningbo to unload the cargo. The barge was piloted by the helmsman, Chen Tianqing, while he himself took the wheel to Ningbo first to wait for the barge to arrive and deliver the cargo. Unfortunately, it was sunk by the New Jiangtian Wheel. After receiving the news, he immediately rushed to Shanghai and specially accompanied Chen Tianqing to report the incident to the bureau.

Could Not Avoid the Collision and Was Sunk:

Chen Tianqing stated that he is the helmsman of the barge, 40 years old, from Huangyan. He has been a helmsman for nearly ten years and was hired to work on this barge last year. On February 14 this year, after loading diesel oil at Texaco at 11 a.m., he sailed to Wusong at 4 p.m. On the 15th, he cleared customs. For several days, he could not sail due to the south wind. At 3 a.m. on the 18th, he set anchor in the northeast wind, sailed along the southern foot of the outer buoy of Songkou, and headed east and south for the exit. He saw a wheel ship moored on his right front, so he sailed past the wheel's bow, about two wheel ship lengths away. Afterwards, he saw a large red light in front of his left, but it was far away, so he continued to proceed along the original route. As he got closer, he knew it was an incoming wheel ship. He immediately turned slightly to the right. Unexpectedly, the wheel also turned to the left. The momentum was very rapid, and no echo was heard. By the time he wanted to avoid, it was too late, and he crashed into the barge's left舷 at the bow.

Eight People Survived, Three Drowned:

After the collision, the bow of the barge immediately sank. At that time, there were a total of eleven crew members on board. Two people were standing at the bow and sank with the wheel ship and drowned immediately. The remaining nine people were at the stern and immediately lowered the sampan to escape. One person did not have time to board the sampan and also sank with the ship. Only eight people survived. The wreckage of the ship flowed along the right舷 of the New Jiangtian Wheel. At that time, the crew members called for help, but the wheel ship ignored them and continued to move forward. The sampan drifted with the tide and was rescued at Wangjiawan in Pudong about an hour later. The whole incident took only half a quarter of an hour and occurred at about 4:30 a.m. that morning. The sailboat had a white square light lit and hanging on the aft cabin shed. At that time, there was a weak northeast wind, and the tide was flat, near the beginning of the tide. According to the bureau, the statement was slightly inconsistent with the New Jiangtian Wheel's report, so the wheel's captain and others will be summoned for questioning again.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 271st inspection report on the issuance reserve of Central Bank exchange coupons states: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, the Bank is responsible for inspecting the number of exchange coupons issued by the Bank and the reserve funds. The 271st inspection was conducted on February 22nd of the 25th year of the Republic of China at the Bank's Issuing Bureau. The inspection results are reported as follows: (A) Total amount of exchange coupons issued: silver dollars 230,440,843 yuan, including silver dollar coupons 207,814,213 yuan, auxiliary coin coupons 22,626,630 yuan. Total exchange coupon reserve: 230,440,843 yuan, including cash reserve silver dollars 163,138,963 yuan. The cash reserve includes 116,820,843.50 yuan stored in the Bank's issuing headquarters and branch libraries, and 46,318,119.49 yuan stored in peer banks. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 67,300,180 yuan in silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold exchange coupons issued: 373,324.70 yuan. Total reserve fund for customs gold exchange coupons: 373,324.70 yuan. The reserve includes 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, which is equivalent to 373,324.70 yuan in customs gold at a price of 50.779. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve should be at least 60%, and the remainder should be guaranteed by legal guarantees. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guaranteed reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This report is hereby issued. February 24, 25th year of the Republic of China, Central Bank: Jian Qing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyin.

The Prospects of Shanghai Xing National Goods Company: Implementing Labor-Capital Cooperation

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor:

Regarding the news published in your esteemed newspaper on February 25th concerning a work slowdown at our factory, upon investigation, it does not align with the facts. Fearing this may mislead the public, we are writing to clarify the situation. We would be grateful if your newspaper could publish the following correction. The calculation of wages for workers in our factory is based on monthly, hourly, and piece-rate systems. Monthly wages are for long-term employees, hourly wages are for short-term employees, and piece-rate wages are for piece-work employees. This is determined based on the work conditions of each worker. This system has been in place since the factory was established and has not been altered in the slightest. Even if we wanted to change it, we are constrained by the realities of the situation. The claim that we recently switched to hourly calculations is entirely untrue. Furthermore, the minimum wage earned by workers each month is fourteen yuan. Diligent workers can earn over twenty yuan per month. If a worker is lazy and earns less, it is their own fault, not the fault of the factory. The claim that each worker earns only three or four yuan per month is also untrue. Upon investigation, the sudden work slowdown by our factory workers was instigated by agitators. They demanded the company accept conditions that had not been approved by party or government authorities, and when this was not met, they incited a full work stoppage to force our hand. The workers claimed the factory stopped providing raw materials as the reason for the second work slowdown, which is absurd. Since the beginning of spring, our factory has been doing well, and work has never been interrupted. Why would we voluntarily abandon business? Furthermore, after the first work slowdown, the workers resumed work after mediation and persuasion by Mr. Lu Yinchu, a representative of the city party headquarters. Their subsequent work stoppage is inconsistent and treats work slowdowns as a game, which is illegal. In addition to reporting this to party and government authorities for a lawful resolution, we are writing this letter to correct the record. We respectfully submit this to the Shenbao News Office. China Fuxin Tobacco Company, February 25th.

To the esteemed Mr. News Editor of the Shenbao News Office: Yesterday's local news section carried a story about a daughter privately arranging a marriage. This is not consistent with the facts, and we are making the following statement to set the record straight. Hui Fu is currently twenty-three years old, having reached the legal age of independence. She was formally engaged to Tu Weijun, who works at the Shanghai YMCA, on the second of this month. Mr. Shan Yinghui, a lawyer, has been engaged to publish a notice to confirm this. The claim that she is only nineteen and privately arranged a marriage is entirely false. Furthermore, she welcomed her mother to live with her in Pudong, but after someone sowed discord, she returned to Shanghai. However, to fulfill her filial duties, she still provides her mother with ten yuan per month for living expenses. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday (February 24th) in the afternoon, she caused trouble at the Labor Elementary School where she works and engaged in physical assault. Under duress, she requested protection from the Public Security Bureau. After mediation, her monthly allowance for living expenses was increased by three yuan. This was out of kindness and not an obligation. Furthermore, her mother had two sons after remarrying, who are now adults and employed, fully capable of supporting her. The claim of stealing private writings is without evidence and is a fabrication. In addition to submitting a statement to the Public Security Bureau for the record to avoid further disputes, we are writing to request your newspaper to make a correction. Respectfully yours, Chen Hui Fu, February 25th, Correspondence Address: Shanghai Pudong YMCA Labor Elementary School

The Tallow and Wax Industry in Shanghai (An Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce - 15)

— Edited by China Credit Information Service

1. History: Tallow and wax is a general term for Chinese tallow, white wax, and paraffin wax. The tallow and wax industry in Shanghai has a long history. For thousands of years, the Chinese people have revered superstition, creating a high demand for candles made from Chinese tallow wax. In 1908, during the late Qing Dynasty, Mr. Yan Zhongshan of the Shanghai Dingfeng Soap Factory and Mr. Chen Hangfan of the Tingli Soap Factory invented the use of Chinese tallow oil in soap making, which then became an industrial raw material. However, at that time, there were very few large-scale soap factories that used Chinese tallow oil. Therefore, before the founding of the Republic of China, the Chinese tallow oil industry still relied on superstition for protection and depended entirely on retail sales for revenue. Since the founding of the Republic, beginning with the Guben Soap Factory in 1921 and the China Soap Company (British Xiangmao Soap Factory) in 1926, which began using Chinese tallow oil, the demand exceeded supply. The number of companies in the same industry gradually increased. In 1931, an unprecedented high price appeared on the market, which influenced the dumping of imported coconut oil and Japanese hardened oil (also known as fish oil). Consequently, sales of tallow soap were almost completely wiped out. In recent years, the price of tallow has dropped again, while the price of imported goods has increased, and sales of tallow are gradually recovering. According to a survey conducted in 1935, the total national tallow oil production was 750,000 dan. In addition to direct consumption, soap sales reached 200,000 dan. Shanghai's tallow oil consumption alone accounted for 92,000 dan. Therefore, this city also plays an important role in the Chinese tallow oil market. Based on the current tallow price, it is difficult for foreign goods to be imported, and the sales of tallow are promising and growing.

Chinese tallow oil and white wax are both unique products of China. In the past, exports to foreign companies were not weak. However, due to the limited uses of these products, they have declined to almost zero today. The decline in production and sales of white wax is particularly severe. Paraffin wax imports began only 30 years ago. The import volume has increased every year. In April 1934, Russian wax first arrived in Shanghai, and the market situation changed. The market has also become sluggish.

2. Types and Origins of Tallow and Wax

Chinese tallow oil is also known as bark oil or white oil. The oil is extracted from the fruit of the Chinese tallow tree. There are many types and names, and the quality varies greatly. Generally, oil from Hubei and Hunan is transported to Shanghai via Hankou and is called "North Oil." Oil from Zhejiang and Anhui is transported to Shanghai via Hangzhou and is called "South Oil." The best oil is white and firm. Oil with a high water content is considered to be inferior. Heavy Jing Oil from Hubei, Jinshi Oil from Hunan, and Heben Oil from Zhejiang are all considered top grade. The most famous brands are Zhu Dashun of Heavy Jing, Wanzipai and Wuzipai of Heben, Yang Chunhe and Heng Yuan Da of Jiangxi Oil, and Wujiadian of Chaxue Oil, which are considered standard brands. In terms of production volume, Macheng Oil is the largest, and Xiang Oil is the smallest. A list of oil names, producing areas, and production volumes is as follows:

White wax is the secretion of wax insects on wax trees. The areas where wax insects and wax trees are produced are different. Wax insects are produced in Qianwei, Ya'an, and Huili, at the border of Sichuan and Yunnan. There are tens of thousands of people who make a living raising wax insects for hundreds of miles. Wax trees are produced in Jiading, Sichuan. During the Lesser Fullness season, the locals transfer the wax insects to the wax trees. The insects eat the wax leaves, and over time, their excrement accumulates and hardens. This is then refined and steamed to become white wax. According to a survey conducted in 1935, the production volume of Jiading Prefecture was 7,000 dan, that of Xuzhou Prefecture was 6,400 dan, and that of Dongchuan, Yunnan, was 2,400 dan, totaling 15,800 dan. Sichuan Province has the highest production volume. The goods can be divided into two types: rice core and general cargo. Rice core is white and firm, while general cargo is bright and loose. The unit is a branch, with eight cakes per branch. The larger cakes weigh 38 jin (city weight) and the smaller ones weigh 19 jin (city weight). The Tianzenggong brand of general cargo and the Qingshenyong brand of rice core are considered the best.

Paraffin wax is also known as mineral wax. It is a byproduct of kerosene, commonly known as petroleum jelly. There are fully refined and semi-refined types, as well as grades of 110, 115, 120, 125, 130, 135, and 140 degrees. The higher the grade, the better the quality. Grades above 135 degrees can be used as raw materials for cosmetics. Candle factories usually use 125-degree goods. The lowest grades are most commonly used by match factories. It is imported from overseas in wooden barrels or burlap sacks. The capacity of the barrels ranges from 350 jin to 400 jin, and the capacity of the burlap sacks ranges from 100 jin to 170 jin. Mobil and Asiatic sell fully refined goods. American goods are mostly semi-refined. Russian goods are all semi-refined. (To be continued)

General Education Situation in Hubei Province in the Past Two Years

Hubei Province's education was extremely dilapidated in the past due to natural disasters and man-made calamities. Since Commissioner Cheng Zhichiu took office in July of the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933], he has strived to reorganize it. After two years of arduous efforts, it is now on track. The following is a summary of the general situation of education at all levels in the province in the past two years.

Education Funding: Since receiving all schools in Hankou City in July of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931], the province's education funding, including provincial schools and libraries, reached more than 330,000 yuan per month. In February of the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932], due to financial difficulties, it was reduced to more than 290,000 yuan. By October of the 21st year, due to the province's insufficient treasury, schools and libraries were closed and merged, and the funding was reduced again. The schools in Hankou City were transferred to the Hankou Municipal Government for management, with a total monthly expenditure of more than 190,000 yuan. By November, it was reduced for the third time, with a monthly expenditure of more than 160,000 yuan. In the 22nd and 23rd years [of the Republic, i.e., 1933 and 1934], to meet the actual needs, the estimated amount was set at more than 170,000 yuan. Including Hankou City's education funding, the annual estimated amount for education and culture in the province, excluding county and district education funding, was 2,650,569 yuan. Excluding Hankou City's education funding, the province's education and culture expenditure for the 23rd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1934] was 2,329,634 yuan (distributed as follows: 134,418 yuan for educational administration, 320,424 yuan for compulsory education, 210,485 yuan for higher education, 927,608 yuan for secondary education, 446,400 yuan for primary schools, 105,502 yuan for social education and cultural undertakings, 64,448 yuan for subsidies and grants, 120,000 yuan for expanding education, and 9,348 yuan for the Office of the Special Commissioner for Education in Western Hubei). All these figures are increased compared to previous years (2,135,172 yuan in the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932] and 2,186,286 yuan in the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933]). The finances of Hubei Province have been affected by years of rampant banditry and communism, which has impacted tax revenues. Even in the first quarter of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931], although it was not abundant, expenditures could still be paid in full each month according to the budget. Since the autumn of that year, due to flooding in the Han River and a decrease in treasury revenue, monthly funding could not be issued on time. Fortunately, starting from November of the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932], after implementing three measures of cutting and merging, revenue and expenditure matched, and monthly funding could be issued twice a month, in the first and second halves of the month. In the past, the accumulated debt to provincial schools and libraries and the funding for studying abroad, which several previous administrations had failed to repay, totaling a huge sum of one million yuan, was actually repaid successively within a year. In the 23rd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1934], the educational undertakings of the province could be promoted to the fullest extent, which was undoubtedly assisted by the fundraising and repayment of accumulated debts. It can also be seen that the educational administration authorities have put in a great deal of effort.

Higher Education: The selection and dispatch of government-funded students to study abroad in our country began in the 11th year of Tongzhi in the Qing Dynasty. The province's government-funded study abroad began in the 25th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, when Zhang Zhidong presided over Hubei's administration. By the 30th year of Guangxu, the number of students sent abroad had reached more than 400. After the establishment of the Republic of China, Li Ming Huangpi supervised Hubei and used revolutionary merits as the standard for sending students abroad. All those who had made meritorious contributions and were talented were sent abroad. Later, in Japan, the standard for selecting and granting government funding was to be admitted to Imperial University, Commercial and Industrial College, Higher Normal School, and the First to Eighth Higher Schools, as well as the Meiji Five Special Schools. Starting from the 6th year of the Republic [i.e., 1917], examinations were used. First, the provincial government held a preliminary examination, and then the Ministry of Education held a re-examination to make a decision. From the 17th to the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1928 to 1933], two types of selection and supplementation were carried out simultaneously. The examination was held domestically. Examinations were held in the 17th, 19th, and 20th years [of the Republic, i.e., 1928, 1930, and 1931], all presided over by the Department of Education, without the need for a re-examination by the Ministry. The supplementation was carried out among self-funded students already studying abroad. From the 17th year to the first semester of the 22nd year, supplementation was carried out whenever there were vacancies. Therefore, most of the government-funded students studying abroad at that time were supplemented. In April of the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933], after the Ministry of Education announced the regulations for studying abroad, the department also revised the regulations for studying abroad and submitted them for approval and implementation. The department, in order to reorganize the funding for studying abroad, in addition to raising funds to repay the previous debts so that government-funded students abroad could study with peace of mind and facilitate assessment, checked that the budget for studying abroad in the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933] was 16,790.40 yuan per month, compiled according to the 90% discount after November of the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932], and the Department of Finance transferred it to the Department of Education each month for remittance to the students. The 23rd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1934] was also compiled according to the 22nd year, with a total annual amount of 201,485.4 yuan, divided into two sections: government-funded students and scholarships for self-funded students. The former received an annual payment of 173,621 yuan, and the latter received an annual payment of 27,864 yuan. In addition, there were temporary expenses for studying abroad, which referred to the expenses for government-funded students' departure, return, travel expenses, medical treatment, compensation, and relief. The annual amount listed in the 23rd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1934] was 1,030 yuan. In order to ensure the stability of the lives of students studying abroad and encourage them to pursue further studies, the department first issued three months' tuition fees to the students who had initially decided to go abroad, and then remitted the fees in advance on a monthly basis from the fourth month onwards. At the same time, it strictly examined their academic performance in order to avoid wasting public funds. According to the latest survey and statistics in the province, there were eight government-funded students in Japan, ten in Germany, three in Belgium, four in England, four in the United States, and one in France. The selection of scholarship students for self-funded study abroad, starting from the 23rd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1934], was carried out by the Department of Education, which appointed Wang Xinggong, Chen Shi, Huang Pu, Jiang Qi, Song Xueting, He Qingming, Gao Qi, and others as review committee members. Ten students, including Wang Zhenhuan, who passed the review, received monthly scholarships ranging from 100 German marks or 30 US dollars to 530 French francs.

Secondary Education: The main points of the secondary education administration in the province in the 22nd and 23rd years [of the Republic, i.e., 1933 and 1934] concerning schools were: holding a provincial conference of secondary school principals, adding simplified normal school courses in Western Hubei and Northern Hubei, expanding the provincial second rural normal school class, deciding to expand vocational school classes and vocational education (the vocational education fee in the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932] was 235,197 yuan, which increased to 396,590 yuan in the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933], and increased to 425,220 yuan in the 23rd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1934], with the goal of reaching the standards set by the Ministry of Education by the 26th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1937]), urging the establishment of agricultural and forestry experiment schools and agricultural and forestry training classes in each administrative commissioner district, ordering all counties to prepare for the establishment of junior vocational schools, reorganizing general secondary schools, developing secondary education in outer districts, and increasing classes so that secondary education in the provincial capital and outer districts, and boys' secondary education and girls' secondary education, could develop equally. Xiangyang Junior High School was added, and the affiliated junior agricultural school of the provincial education college was added in the old year, as well as the provincial second rural normal girls' vocational normal class and the provincial third rural normal girls' vocational class. Regarding faculty and staff, the focus was on reviewing qualifications, assessing performance, improving treatment, implementing guarantees, holding secondary school science, history, and geography seminars, and preparing for the certification of secondary normal school teachers. Regarding students, the focus was on reducing the burden on students (exempting tuition fees and book fees, and stipulating that the cost of uniforms should not exceed four yuan in winter and three yuan in summer, and the registration fee should not exceed five jiao. All miscellaneous fees, loss fees, and boarding fees not stipulated in the secondary school regulations were not allowed to be charged), setting up scholarships for poor students (40 high school students, 40 yuan per student per year; 120 junior high school students, 30 yuan per student per year), reviewing students' academic performance in each school, holding speech contests, holding graduation exams and regular spot checks, and strictly implementing junior high school scouting training and high school student training, etc.

Primary Education: The province's primary education was previously considered good by Zhong Daozan, section chief of the Ministry of Education's inspectorate, and Wu Yan Yin. The students' performance in the two subjects of Mandarin and labor was the best. The more important matters handled in the 22nd and 23rd years [of the Republic, i.e., 1933 and 1934] were: designating provincial Wuxue Primary School and other schools as central primary schools in Eastern Hubei, Western Hubei, and Northern Hubei, holding summer seminars for primary school teachers, ordering all primary schools to focus on labor classes to cultivate children's operating habits and production skills, reducing the burden on students in each primary school, and exempting tuition fees in provincial schools and adding restrictions to private schools, and setting up free places for more than one-third of students to help poor children), dividing the provincial Wuchang experimental district into junior primary school guidance districts, setting up guidance directors, and designating five schools to pilot the two-part system, establishing a provincial primary education research association and discussing primary education issues, adding classes to provincial primary schools and normal school-affiliated primary schools, and adding kindergartens and provincial compulsory education experimental districts, short-term primary schools, and simplified primary schools.

Local Education: In the past, education in Hubei Province inevitably emphasized the provincial capital and neglected local areas, with a vast difference in levels. After Commissioner Cheng's two years of determined reorganization and promotion, the larger matters were as follows: 1. Holding a provincial county and district education administration conference to properly plan the improvement of local education; 2. Implementing the Hubei Revival of Local Education Three-Year Plan to save the decline of local education; 3. Implementing the measures for revitalizing local education in Western Hubei in order to achieve the average development of education in Western Hubei and all counties in Hubei; 4. Reviewing and certifying primary school teachers, eliminating the inferior and reusing normal school graduates to improve the content of local schools; 5. Registering county supervisors to carefully select local education inspectors and guides; 6. Formulating the regulations of the Hubei County Private School Teacher Certification Committee and the regulations of the Private School Teacher Summer Training Class to certify and train private school teachers and improve private schools; 7. Formulating the Hubei Regulations on Rewarding Donations to Schools to reward private individuals and private groups for establishing schools; 8. Formulating the Hubei Regulations on the Retirement of Education Administrative Personnel to encourage education administrative personnel and promote the advancement of local education; 9. Merging all non-abolished education bureaus into the third section of the county government and temporarily approving the collection of education surcharges according to the existing plan to save administrative expenses, expand local education undertakings, and maintain existing local education matters without interruption; 10. Formulating the Hubei Outline of Measures for Implementing the Integration of Politics and Education and Popularizing Education and the Measures for Establishing Primary Schools by Joint Guarantee in Each County to seek the active development of local education and the coordinated progress of politics and education. Except for the tenth item, which only began to be implemented in June of the 24th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1935], the remaining items have all had considerable results. Taking only primary education as an example, according to the latest survey, there are a total of 4,300 primary schools and junior primary schools in each county of the province, with 1,200 added in the 22nd and 23rd years [of the Republic, i.e., 1933 and 1934], accounting for about one-third of the total number. This shows that local education has shown signs of revival after two years of management, which shows the efforts of the provincial education administration authorities.

In addition, the province has adopted special education for adults, children, and adult women in the recovered bandit areas, widely established mass schools and mass education halls, agricultural education halls, and adopted mobile teaching and traveling lecture methods, improved mass entertainment and customs, and universally implemented physical education, rectified the academic atmosphere, and promoted academic research. There are many such undertakings with remarkable achievements. Due to space limitations, they are all omitted.

Financials: Gold Bar Market Experiences Rebound, Recovering One Yuan From Previous Decline

The gold market, which had been under pressure and weakening due to continuous selling pressure, experienced a slight rebound yesterday. Surprisingly, the increase in the price of foreign silver was not satisfactory. Some buyers took advantage of the low prices to purchase, but the overall trend remained extremely sluggish. In the early morning, overseas silver markets indicated rises in both British and American markets. Large traders speculated that there would be sellers following the closing price quotations. Distant-term silver prices in Montreal rose by varying amounts, from one to four-and-three-tenths of a cent. Exchange rates generally increased. London gold spot prices fell by half a penny. The Central Bank's posted exchange rates showed no change for both the British and American currencies. The Customs Gold Unit remained unchanged. The standard gold bar price was posted at 1,146.6 yuan, stabilizing market sentiment. Off-exchange pre-market trading opened at around 45.5 yuan. The morning opening was slightly higher, but prices initially declined slightly after opening. However, with increased buying interest, prices quickly rebounded. Supply increased as prices rose. HSBC's posted exchange rates showed no change for both the British and American currencies. At this point, prices fluctuated rapidly and remained unstable. The posted silver equalization tax remained unchanged and had little impact. Later in the day, larger traders made slight advances, causing a slight increase in prices. Unexpectedly, retail investors aggressively entered the market, hindering the upward trend. As a result, the situation at midday remained one of fluctuation. The market subsequently became stagnant again. Prices were slightly stable after opening, but it was difficult to raise prices further, even with many sellers eager to unload their holdings. Prices gradually declined. The market was extremely quiet in the middle of the day, mainly due to the sluggishness of the foreign exchange market. Reports from the Indian silver market indicated a decrease of two annas. Finally, there was no further change. The spot price was 5.6 yuan below the four-month forward price. The three-month forward price rose to over 4.5 yuan above the four-month price. The day's market conditions are recorded below:

The morning opening was 1,145.7 yuan, a recovery of six cents from the previous close. Hong Kang Yong Heng and others sold slightly, lowering the price to 5.3 yuan. Ding Kang, Ri Chang, Da De Cheng, Fu Xing, Yong Shun Mao, and Da Fa continuously purchased bars, raising the price to 6.6 yuan. Da De Cheng, Fu Xing, Yong Heng Yu, and Hui Xiang sold late in the day, retreating the price to 6.1 yuan. HSBC's posted exchange rates remained unchanged for both British and American currencies. Da De Cheng, Ri Chang, and Yuan Yi advanced to 6.7 yuan. Da De Cheng, Yuan Mao, Yong Ding Kang, and others sold at 6.1 yuan. The posted silver equalization tax remained unchanged and had little impact. Ri Chang, Yong De Ju, Da Fu Xing Yong, and others raised the price of bars back to 6.8 yuan. Unexpectedly, retail investors aggressively entered the market. Da Chang Xiang and others also sold, gradually reducing the price to 6 yuan. Da De Cheng maintained prices while taking advantage of the lower prices. Yuan Mao Yong sold slightly and the price fluctuated. The closing price at midday was 1,146.1 yuan.

The afternoon opening was 1,146.3 yuan. Zhi Chang sold slightly, retreating the price to 6.2 yuan. Hui Xiang, Ri Chang, Shen Da Yong purchased bars, raising the price to 6.4 yuan. Ri Chang, Da Feng Heng, Da De Cheng and others sold, gradually retreating the price to 6 yuan. Initial reports from the Indian silver market indicated a decrease of two annas. Hui Xiang immediately sold after purchasing. Da De Cheng also sold. After fluctuating, the closing price was 1,146.1 yuan. The market was stable after the close.

The closing price, based on the Central Bank's posted gold bar price, was 1,146.6 yuan. Compared to the opening and closing prices, this represents a decrease of approximately half a yuan, and a decrease of over one yuan from the previous closing price. The bookkeeping price for March was 1,141 yuan, and for April it was 1,146 yuan. The water supplement in the morning was 1,141 yuan, and the same price in the afternoon. The price of refined gold, based on the forward price, increased by two yuan, to 1,147.7 yuan. The spot market conditions were stable. Tianjin goods were sold with a premium of 9.5 yuan. Refined gold with a premium of 9 yuan was lacking counterparties. The spot price was 5.6 yuan below the four-month forward price for those unwinding their positions. Those unwinding their positions included Da Feng Heng with 56 bars, Sheng Yuan and Yong with 49 bars, Ying Feng Heng with 49 bars, Qian Chang Xiang with 42 bars, and Da De Cheng with 35 bars, all of which were purchased by Da Chang Xiang.

For the March to April period, Yuan Mao Yong paid Da Chang Xiang 28 bars at 4.5 yuan. Fu Yu paid Ying Feng Heng 35 bars, and Yuan Mao Yong paid Tong Feng Heng 7 bars at 4.6 yuan. Yi Cheng paid Hui Xiang at 4.7 yuan. In the afternoon market, Da De Cheng paid Yuan Mao Yong 35 bars at 4.7 yuan.

Trading within the market was average. In summary, Jin Feng Yong Fu Yu Wan Feng Qing Fa Yong Chun Yuan Yong Fu Xing Yong Heng Yu Yong De Ju Da Shen Da Yong Qia Feng, Yong Hui Xiang and others were on the buying side. Da De Cheng, Ri Chang Xiang He, Ding Kang Yuan Mao Yong Feng Chang Qian Yuan Yong and others were on the selling side. Ri Chang, Da De Cheng, and Ding Kang were early buyers and late sellers. Heng Yu and Yuan Mao Yong were early sellers and late buyers.

The day's market conditions were average. The morning opening was 1,145.7 yuan, and the closing price was 1,146.1 yuan. The highest price was 1,146.8 yuan, and the lowest price was 1,145.3 yuan, a fluctuation of one and a half yuan. The result was an increase of one yuan compared to the previous closing. The total number of transactions for the day was 4,060 bars in the morning and 861 bars in the afternoon. There were still 5,971 March forward contracts remaining. In total, there were 19 long parties and 22 short parties. The total number of April forward contracts was 11,074 bars. In total, there were 62 long parties and 30 short parties.

Foreign Exchange: British Market Flat, American Market Looser

The foreign exchange market yesterday lacked excitement as Chinese merchants remained inactive. The result was a flat British market and a looser American market. In the early morning, foreign telegrams indicated that the London large-lot forward market was unchanged in the near term and up 0.0625 in the long term. It was said on the floor that there would be sellers following the closing price quotations. The New York silver market was unchanged. Distant-term silver prices in Montreal rose by varying amounts, from one to four-and-three-tenths of a cent. London gold spot prices decreased by half a penny. The British currency rose against the American currency by 0.875. The British currency rose against the French currency by 19 pounds. The American currency rose against the British currency by 0.875. The American currency rose against the French currency by 0.25. The Central Bank's posted exchange rates showed no change for both the British and American currencies. The Customs Gold Unit remained unchanged. After the opening, banks engaged in mutual trading. HSBC's posted exchange rates showed no change for both the British and American currencies and remained stable. The posted silver equalization tax remained unchanged. Bank mutual trading of exchange rates made the process even more ordinary. At midday, there was no change due to the differing appetites of banks. In the afternoon, market sentiment was calm and banks remained on the sidelines. As a result, in addition to mutual trading, speculative trading was lacking and the process was stagnant. Finally, although Indian silver fell by two annas, it had no impact. The long-term market was the same, due to the general increase in exchange rates. Chinese merchants lacked activity, and banks mostly engaged in mutual trading. Securities: Eighth Round of Unified Government Bonds Trading — Regulations Announced by the Exchange

The Chinese Stock Exchange completed the February futures settlement by the 27th. On the 28th, the exchange announced the commencement of spot trading in various Unified Government Bonds, largely consistent with past practice. The previous restriction on the submission of physical goods has been effectively lifted. The Exchange's two announcements are listed below:

(1) The Board of Directors has resolved to implement spot trading in Unified Government Bonds, etc., for the March and April periods starting February 28th. The implementation measures and the Ministry of Finance's announcement of the Unified Government Bond regulations and amortization schedule are listed below (table omitted). In addition to notifying the brokers' association, this is hereby announced.

Spot trading in five types of Unified Government Bonds (A, B, C, D, E) and March and April futures trading will be implemented. Spot trading in these bonds is denominated in units of 1,000 yuan. Futures trading is denominated in units of 5,000 yuan. Spot trading in these bonds will be conducted in accordance with Exchange Announcement No. 709. For every 10,000 yuan of March and April futures trading in these bonds, each party must pay a margin of 100 yuan in cash and 400 yuan in special margin. Bonds with a face value of 5,000 yuan may be used for delivery at settlement, along with those with a face value of 1,000 yuan. These bonds may be used as collateral for margin and guarantees in trading. The price fluctuation limit for these bonds is 4 yuan above or below the previous day's bookkeeping price. Trading will be temporarily suspended to allow for margin calls. The aforementioned measures will be implemented from the 28th of this month.
