Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Microorganism)

If the cook draws water from the well, and the water-drawing tools are incomplete, with only a bucket but no bucket rope, how can the well water be drawn ashore to cook and prepare meals? Therefore, when drinking water, one should remember the source. We cannot but give credit to the bucket rope for its drawing power. Nowadays, when people are unemployed, they ask others for help to be raised up, speaking flowery and delightful words, absolutely not forgetting the kindness of the support. But once they are placed in a position, or later develop a little, they look down upon everything, not even putting the person who helped them in the past in their eyes. Such ungrateful friends are everywhere in the world. One must know, when eating rice, don't forget the farmer!

Furthermore, sometimes the bucket rope is very thick and strong, originally capable of drawing up a lot, but what is used is a broken bucket with holes. Then it is terrible, a full bucket of water drawn up will undoubtedly leak half of it, or all of it. This cannot be blamed on the bucket rope's ineffectiveness, but should be attributed to the bucket's own worthlessness. Therefore, promotion - assistance, also needs to be accurate. Help if it is worth it, otherwise, acting arbitrarily, you might waste your effort!

Sentries of Outer Mongolia

— Zi Ying

At a time when Japanese-Soviet relations are extremely tense, with war a distinct possibility, the conflict in Manchuria and Mongolia, which is the outpost of these two major powers, is becoming increasingly acute. Here, we probably all feel the allure of Outer Mongolia's border defenses.

I have a friend who used to do business in the Chahar-Suiyuan area. Recently, due to the rampant "bandits," he packed up and returned south. He told me a story about Outer Mongolian sentries. Now I will write it down, the following are his words:

"Three years ago, it was late summer and early autumn. Encouraged by friends, for the sake of a little profit, I disregarded all difficulties and dangers and resolved to sneak into Outer Mongolia.

"The weather outside the Great Wall is very bad, especially in the desert. During the day, the sun burns people like a ball of fire, and the temperature is often above ninety degrees. But at night, it is terribly cold, and you must cover yourself with two layers of felt. We traveled in such desolate wilderness, having crossed the boundless desert for five days. We had reached the border of Outer Mongolia, and still hadn't seen a single person. We were celebrating the success of our smuggling, but the next day we were caught by their patrol sentries.

"As I said just now, the border of Outer Mongolia is a desert. Their sentries patrol using this desert. They all ride fine horses, galloping back and forth. They drag a leafy branch behind the horse. When the horse runs, the leaves drag on the ground, making the desert very smooth. People walking on the sand are bound to leave tracks, and they follow the tracks. Nine times out of ten, they catch someone.

"Have you all read the Romance of the Three Kingdoms, seen Zhang Yide fighting Cao Cao at Dangyang Bridge? Didn't he order his soldiers to tie branches to the horses and gallop through the woods, making dust fly into the sky, as a ruse? I didn't expect the Outer Mongolian patrol sentries to also use these leaves."

"At first, they thought we were spies and guarded us very closely. But the food and lodging were very good. Later, when they learned that we were all merchants, they escorted us out of the country."

The Beginning of Establishing Schools to Teach English

— Yi Mei

Shanghai is a major trading port. European ships come from the east, and trade is prosperous. Chinese people have set up schools to teach English, and young people flock to them. Although English has now been included as a major subject in schools, and everyone can study it, the advertisements for English cram schools are still conspicuous in the streets. Examining its beginnings, it was in the first month of the second year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty. At that time, everyone in the country considered discussing foreign affairs to be fashionable. Li Shaoquan (Li Hongzhang) was considered to be one who knew foreign affairs well, and he established the so-called Foreign Languages Institute in Shanghai. At the time, there was a memorial to the throne, which said: "I humbly believe that when China interacts with foreigners, it must first understand their intentions, communicate their meanings, and know their truthfulness and falsehoods, and then can there be an effective application of appropriate measures. Among our officials and gentry, very few are proficient in foreign languages. Each country in Shanghai has established one or two translators. When Chinese and foreign ministers meet to discuss matters, they all rely on foreign translators to convey the information, and it is difficult to guarantee that there will be no bias or fabrication. Chinese people who are proficient in foreign languages rely only on interpreters. When dealing with foreign affairs, the weight, tone, and urgency of the words are often lost in the original intent. They only know how to use the power of foreigners to play tricks and instigate disputes for their own benefit. Foreign affairs are an important policy for the country to cherish and attract distant people, but entrusting the key to the hands of such people leads to not knowing the other party and not distinguishing between truth and falsehood. Manipulating advances and retreats, they never get to the point. This is no small matter. Shanghai and Guangdong are the places where foreigners gather the most. I humbly propose that we follow the example of the Tongwen Guan in Beijing and add a Foreign Languages Institute in Shanghai. Select literate children under the age of fourteen from nearby counties, who are intelligent and of good character, and hire Westerners to teach them. After three or five years, we will have people who are educated and reasonable, proficient in foreign languages. For the offices of the trading commissioners and governors, and the customs superintendents, we should add translators, and those who handle foreign affairs should be selected from the institute," etc. The original text is very long, this is a summary of it.

Fruit Vendor

Chess Talk

— Yang Yu Sheng

Lately, I haven't talked about romance for a long time, but I play Weiqi every night, and I even have the spare time to write this chess talk for this publication. I can truly be considered to be "in between classes"!

Confucius once said: "The gentleman does not contend over anything, only his heart is focused on archery." Even with the morality and cultivation of a gentleman, he cannot be free from contention. So, if we have disputes or even quarrels because of playing chess, it is not surprising from a gentleman's point of view!

People often play Chinese chess in barbershops, so they add the word "stinky" to "Chinese chess", calling it "stinky Chinese chess." But according to Chinese historical records, Xie An, the "patriarch of pure conversation," was still calmly playing Weiqi when his nephews were "killing bandits and establishing merit" at the Fei River. Even the two star lords of the North and South Poles also play Weiqi in their spare time. The fact that Chinese chess is not valued by the literati or even the celestial realm has a long history!

Recently, someone told me an anecdotal joke: It is said that in one place, two people were playing Weiqi upstairs, and a lot of people were gathered downstairs playing Chinese chess. The latter often quarreled, making all sorts of unpleasant noises due to disputes. Therefore, one bystander sighed and said, "Playing Weiqi is really elegant. Listen, have you heard any noise upstairs? Only you playing stinky Chinese chess would make such a loud and nasty racket!" Later, "when the time was up," the Chinese chess game was declared over, but the two people upstairs were not seen coming down. So, someone ran upstairs to check. It turned out that they were desperately gripping each other's throats, fighting to the death!

We won't discuss whether this joke is me teasing the people who play Weiqi. Just speaking in terms of "human nature," the more knowledge people have, the bigger and more fierce their conflicts will be! The "rotten talk" that "the gentleman does not contend" is "this road is blocked" in the 20th century!

Notes on What I Saw

— (Zhang Mengzhao)

Can it be considered folklore?

Once when using the toilet, I happened to see a limerick written in pencil on the partition wall, which was very interesting. I don't know who wrote it? The poem says:

A virgin is born beautiful,

With a pair of small feet,

She is thirty-three years old,

Do you want her or not?

Old People Under the Wheels

"The road is like a tiger's mouth, do not walk in the middle." Living in a city full of thorns, everyone knows and remembers these two sentences. But last Sunday afternoon at noon, I witnessed an old man being knocked down by a public bus driver. The old man was carrying rice, and the rice was scattered on the ground. Pitifully, he fell flat on his back, almost losing his life. Bystanders were indignant and chased after the bus, cursing wildly. But the driver knew he had caused trouble, and the bus drove even faster. Everyone was helpless and could only watch the old man groan and struggle to get up from the ground. This happened on Yangshupu Road near the Bund. The driver deliberately committed a mistake and sped away in a hurry. Is there really any reason to be found in Shanghai? This matter does not seem to be the fault of the elderly who are old and deaf.

Little Western Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 24: Weighting Profit Over Beauty, a Laborer Reluctantly Gives Up Love; With High Aspirations and Healthy Legs, a Brave Man Ventures into the Wilderness

Zhiqian said you've been busy all morning and haven't even seen the newspaper, what have you been doing? Bei Hai looked at Zhang Jiefu and smiled: This matter... I'll report back later. Following this situation, Zhang Jiefu nodded and left. Zhiqian laughed: I already know what you were talking about. I was also having lunch over there just now and heard Old Jia's words. You are a bit silly, why did you refuse his contribution? Bei Hai blushed and said: Mr. Cheng heard it, this is a bit inappropriate. Zhiqian poured a cup of tea, stood at the corner of the table, held it in his hands, slowly drank it, his eyes looking at Bei Hai's face from the heat circle of the teacup, shaking his head with a smile: What you said is a bit inappropriate, maybe it's exactly appropriate. Bei Hai tilted his head to look back at Zhiqian, pressed his hands on his thighs, tapped his feet on the ground and smiled: Mr. Cheng thinks this matter is a bit possible. Zhiqian said: To be honest, Mr. Jia's purpose in marrying this Miss Zhu is only to have some temporary fun because life in the Little Western Heaven hotel is too lonely, he found Miss Zhu to accompany him. But for this little thing, it caused the women's world to attack him collectively. The loss of love is a small matter, but it has a huge impact on the cause he is carrying out in Xi'an. He represents the bank's investment here. If his reputation is ruined and things don't work out, it doesn't matter if he loses face in Xi'an, but when he returns to Shanghai and Nanjing, he will also lose face. This is closely related to the problem of livelihood. You must know that in this day and age, all problems have an economic background. Probably he first couldn't get by, inevitably his emotions were stirred up, and he quarreled with people. Afterwards, he thought about it carefully and realized that he couldn't spoil his livelihood for the sake of temporary courage, it's better to be patient and let Miss Zhu leave. Since this person can't hold on to it, why not have you as an introducer. You are grateful to him, maybe you will help him a little in selling land. After thinking it through, this is still beneficial to him, so he had those words. Zhiqian said the words while sipping tea, looking at Bei Hai, constantly deepening his smile on his face, as if he had already recalled it. Then he came over and patted Bei Hai on the shoulder and said: If you are willing to trust me and listen to me, I can let you lovers get married. (408)

Small Gardening

Potting Plum Cultivation Method (Middle)

— Hu Chuyu

Watering: The amount of flowering in potted plums is greatly related to the appropriateness of watering. For ordinary cultivation of trees, it is advisable to water more. To produce more flowers, it cannot be neglected. If too little water is given, the flowers will wither, and the growth of the tree will also be affected. The four words "more fertilizer, less moisture" are the secret to producing more flowers. Originally, plums like sunny places and also like dry places. Every year from the beginning of budding in early April to before the plum rain season, apply fertilizer fully and use less water, which is to promote vigorous budding. The thickness of the leaves determines the flower buds. Thin leaves will not produce flowers. Plum leaves absorb a lot of water when they grow, and the soil in the pot is easy to dry. The water poured in the morning should be dry by the evening. If we see that the soil in the pot has turned white, we should water it. The number of times to water each day is once a day in spring and autumn, twice a day in midsummer, and once every few days in winter. If there is too much water, then the buds will fall off, and the branches will easily grow longer. (To prevent the branches from growing too long, the bud tips can be cut off)

The quality of plum blossom branches is determined before the plum rain season, and its flower buds are also fixed. Young trees should be made to flower more. At the end of March, the soil in the pot should be temporarily dried. Old trees should not do this. After the flower buds are fixed, the water should be used appropriately. After the leaves fall, the water absorption is less, and watering should be slow. As for the water used, well water and river water are the most suitable, tap water should not be used. Winter ice water is also not suitable because the temperature is too low. Usually, mild clean water should be used so as not to harm the roots.

The Place to Put the Plum

It should be placed in a ventilated and sunny place. If it is placed in a windless and semi-shady place, it will only cause the branches to grow, and the flower core will not be bright, and it will easily suffer from pests and diseases. In midsummer, do not put it in a semi-shady place, it can be exposed to the scorching sun. When the wind is strong, prevent the soft branches from shaking, or the friction between branches. If the planting is very dense, thin bamboo can be used to support it so that they do not touch. Also, during periods of prolonged rain, it should be moved under the eaves.

Pruning and Thin Wire

After flowering, the branches and leaves should be pruned. The new axes of young trees are easy to lengthen, and one or two buds can be left at the base of the new shoots, and the useless branches and leaves can be trimmed according to the posture of the buds. However, there are also cases where the excessively long new shoots are cut off in summer. Although new buds can grow on the cut branches, these buds will not produce flowers, so it is better not to cut them. The new buds of old trees, if they grow only two or three points long, do not need to be cut off. However, because the tender branches and old branches are juxtaposed, it looks very inelegant, so it is better to cut them off. When the plum branches reach the plum rain season, the branches are very soft, and the plum branches can be coiled with wire according to the desired appearance, but the wire should be wrapped in paper. To correct ancient branches, hemp can be wrapped on the branches and slowly corrected. If you want to carve words or paintings on the plum trunk, or treat bark cracks, that must be done in March of spring.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Tragic Incident at Tianjin Warm Shelter

— Xin Xin

According to recent reports from Tianjin, the tragic fire at the warm shelter is truly unbearable to read. What we see are only news reports and photos, and we already feel this way. If we had witnessed the tragedy firsthand or visited the site afterward, the impressions of sadness and horror would be ten or a hundred times greater.

The interior of the warm shelter was constructed entirely of flammable materials, which was already extremely dangerous. This "flammable" warm shelter was "locked with straw mats at night" and "had no management personnel." It was foreseeable that a fire would cause such an unprecedented tragedy.

Charitable endeavors can only passively prevent the poor from resorting to desperate measures, as clearly demonstrated in this incident. Moreover, if there are "charity hustlers" who "build their fortunes on charity," what is the value of charitable endeavors in society? It is self-evident that we need not say more.

Charitable endeavors only alleviate the emotions of the poor, as clearly demonstrated in this incident (as evidenced by the fact that "the poor regarded it as a blessed place and competed to live in the shelter! Even in the severe cold, they were very comfortable, and even rickshaw pullers and vendors abandoned their professions to live there"). However, what are the consequences of these passive effects? They cultivate the laziness of the poor. If you don't believe it, there is evidence: "After the Mingde warm shelters and the Huashang Gonghui's porridge distribution centers for men and women were completely burned down this morning, the poor men and women who relied on the porridge were unable to eat because the porridge centers were burned down. At the same time, they had no place to stay at night because the warm shelters were burned down. The poor were greatly disappointed."

It is a fact that without the establishment of porridge distribution centers, some of the poor would starve or freeze to death in the "severe cold." However, it is also inevitable that they would find a way to survive in order to fight against death. What is the difference between acquiring this survival skill and the current situation of "being unable to eat" and "having no place to stay" after the fire? Anyone with clear eyes can see this, and we need not belabor the point. Even if we step back and say that it provides a "very comfortable" "blessed place" for the poor in the "severe cold" to show a slight intention of "sharing happiness with the people," then these two warm shelters are simply too few. There are many people under the heavens (even in a small place like Tianjin) who want to enjoy a "very comfortable" "blessed place"!

Perhaps some would say that charitable endeavors are a desperate measure under the current social system, and that this measure is still most beneficial to the poor before the entire social system is thoroughly reformed. However, I still cannot remain silent because after the "major disaster," some people "held a mass for over a hundred victims and asked monks and Taoists to chant sutras to deliver their souls" at the First Branch Bureau. This kind of foolish and absurd thing is by no means the most beneficial to the poor.

What else can we talk about!

Old Residence

— Luo Zhihua

Lin Zibin was a fellow filled with fantasy and memories, his life seemed only to be for past enchantments.

I knew him from four years ago, after the September 18th Incident, in an apartment in Beiping. At that time, Beiping was like a crab being scalded by boiling water, with turmoil every day, and fear dominating the world. The ancient air of the past was awakened by the cold current that swept in from outside Shanhaiguan. Not only did the air clear people's minds, but the painful faces of the people fleeing from outside the關, also made people understand what kind of drama was about to be staged.

At that time, I was studying in Beiping, and after class, I often went to play at my fellow villager's place. One time, I ran into Lin Zibin.

His slender body had a small head on top, which didn't look very pleasing. Everything else was fine, his hair was black and shiny, and his eyes were bright and quick. His lips were as bright as if they had been painted with lipstick. He spoke in a low, delicate, feminine tone.

The first time I met him, I was a little unhappy: he had no backbone. So I didn't talk much. Later, my fellow villager told me: this guy had just run back from the Northeast and was preparing to study liberal arts at our school. The second time I saw him, I lowered my voice like an elementary school teacher trying to coax the truth out of a student, and said:

"Are you planning to enter the school, Mr. Lin?"

He turned around in surprise from "fantasy and memories," parted his bright lips, smiled, and said, "I am preparing to enter the liberal arts department of your school."

"Oh," I replied, staring at his movements with both eyes. He seemed afraid of me, his face was a little red, and his hands and feet couldn't find a suitable place to put them. When I noticed this, I quickly shifted my gaze to my fellow villager who was sketching, and said at the same time, "That's great, we have another companion!" He only smiled shyly.

Later, because the school organized a petition group to go south to Nanjing, we all participated, and we had more opportunities to talk, so we became familiar with each other.

In the petition group, because he was from the Northeast, he was particularly enthusiastic and crazy. He was excited every day, his little red face shouting:

"As long as the government sends troops to recover the lost territory according to what I think, I am willing to go back and be a soldier! ... You don't know how vast the grasslands of the Northeast are..."

Whenever he had free time, he would tell us about the situation in the Northeast. To supplement his inadequate descriptions, he would also show us five or six neatly arranged photo albums. Most of them were landscape photos and photos of his family. In these photos, he loved a small Western-style house standing in a garden the most. Every time he saw that picture, he would repeat it again and again without any sense of vulgarity:

"This is where I live." He pointed to the picture, as if he was immersed in memories again: "The scenery around here is really good. Looking out, it's a vast plain. In winter, it's all white snow, and in summer, it's all green grass. This house of mine is right here. It was built by my father when he was a brigade commander. He specifically told me to live in it. ... Alas, you don't know, the roof of this house is red tiles, and how well it matches the surrounding scenery! ... Like a bright red flower, standing in the green leaves... I have eight hundred Japanese literary books, all placed in this room, and my unfinished masterpiece "I am Hesitating in the Vast Northern Wilderness" is also placed in this room... But it's all gone during the September 18th Incident..."

He held the photo album, immersed in memories and fantasies.

Not only was he like this, but several young masters who came with him were also like this. At that time, their articles often appeared in the supplements of Beiping newspapers. The content of the articles was about missing their desolate Manchurian plains. Whether it was prose or poetry, the content of Lin Zibin's "I am Hesitating in the Vast Northern Wilderness" was also like this.

So later, when we saw Lin Zibin, we would say, "Have you written any memories recently?"

"No," another person said, "He's all in fantasy, he's fantasizing about his home being a hundred times more beautiful than before!"

He smiled shyly and said, "No, no, no, I'm just too, too, ... too sad! Too melancholic!"

In Nanjing, he was also very sad. When he saw a red house, he would say, "Alas, it looks so much like my house! ... When will I be able to see it again! ... That beautiful house, that desolate Manchuria, the lover's Manchuria!" He whistled softly and sighed!

But he had no choice but to live in an apartment in Beiping. He sent letters to his family, but his family didn't reply. He only had an elderly father. At the same time, life became more and more difficult. The more bitter life was, the sweeter the beautiful dreams of the past felt.

Four years passed quickly, and his life was completely built on writing a few articles. It was said that he had simply become dear friends with poverty in a month.

Last winter, I went to Beiping in a hurry to see my brother at school, and at the same time, I met with classmates I hadn't seen for a long time. I also saw him. His lips were already pale, his face was no longer rosy, and he was even thinner. Compared with his body, which seemed stubbornly long, it was even more disproportionate. His hands seemed to have only a few bones left. I shook his hand tightly and said:

"How's life?"

"Me," he was still as if immersed in memories: "It's still the same old story! ..."

I asked a friend, and the friend told me that his father had been killed by the ×× people because he was unwilling to be a traitor. Lin Zibin, then, became even more melancholy, and even less able to pull his feet out of the mire of fantasy and memories. Now he only hopes that one day a war will break out. He said, "I will definitely go to the front line!"

Nonsense

— (Fool)

The newspaper reported the other day that the negotiations in eastern Hebei have made "progress," and Yin will go to Peiping to take office, and the puppet organization will be abolished without any problems. Old Man Tan said, what is the so-called "progress," is it progress on the Japanese side? Or progress on our side? Although the puppet organization can be abolished, I am a little afraid of this famous Mr. Yin coming to Beiping.

The newly appointed Ambassador to China, Arida, brought a new policy towards China, with two points: 1. Based on the Three Principles, gradually concretize them; 2. Unify diplomacy, and coordinate foreign affairs with the military. We have already learned the Three Principles of Foreign Minister Hirota, and now we need to see how they are concretized and how foreign affairs are coordinated with the military! We Chinese should open our eyes and see.

Xu Wenbi's Opening

City Sound (1340) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Opening of Faded Red"

Where does the official boat moor in the river? . A mad autumn wind is chilling. A virtuous Sima of Jiangzhou sits above. In the seat, the wine spirit is very high. At that time. Distinguished guests and virtuous hosts were all seated. Not even knowing. Poems and songs were offered for jokes. At this moment. There was a woman of elegance on the neighboring boat. Only heard. The sad pipa played a song. Did not know. That old lady Qiuniang was still beautiful and enchanting. Also. Her voice was gentle, veiled. It was said that her name was Hua Tui Hong, showing infinite shame in front of guests. With head lowered, she had no words to speak. And tried to ask the past. She said. That when she was small, she was leaning on the door and selling charm. Staying close to dance fans and singing gowns. Soon. There were few carriages and horses in front of the door. Looking back, there was no home to return to. So she married a merchant's wife. But her husband went to Fuliang and had not returned yet. This lead to. Her loneliness as a swan dancing alone with its shadow. She could only use old artistic skills to earn a living. She did it. Only to make a meager living as family expenses were difficult. It was not that the red-face was thin-fated. But instead, she pitied her own status to the loss of her hairpin. Unexpectedly. It drew tears from the Jiangzhou Sima. And dampened the green shirt. Originally. Affectionate people were very talented. With a broken heart, he sighed three times. Not fearing the reward of his own waist. And hurried home at the end of night. With lamp lit, unable to sleep, she felt bored. She wrote a Pipa and her tears had not dried. And through the windows the setting sun was a curved hook.

Movie News

Gu Lan Jun and Wang Zhengxin Officially Married

— Ye Ke

Gu Lan Jun, one of the leading ladies in the "Peach and Plum Vie for Glory," indeed formally married Wang Zhengxin, the stalwart young actor, the day before yesterday. Details are recorded as follows:

Secret Before the Wedding The love between Gu Lan Jun and Wang Zhengxin has been rumored for a long time. However, director Li Pingqian denied it. Therefore, it was not confirmed until after the wedding the day before yesterday afternoon. Director Li Pingqian remained tight-lipped two hours before Gu and Wang's wedding. This is how secret a female star's wedding can be.

Preparation Before the Wedding At noon the day before yesterday, the staff of the Star Film Company's No. 2 studio were very busy. The Star Film Company's No. 1 car went to a shop on Jing'an Temple Road to purchase a large bouquet of fresh flowers, worth ten silver dollars, for the bride Gu Lan Jun. There was also a large pile of small fresh flowers and a large package of paper flowers for the guests. The bride went to a large fashion company in the morning to try on her wedding dress. The groom, Wang Zhengxin, also had a shave and bath. The administrative staff also actively prepared for the wedding ceremony that day.

Guests Gathered The clock struck twelve. Two large trucks carrying male and female guests, totaling more than one hundred, arrived in front of the Star Film Company's No. 2 studio. They were dressed in colorful attire and were very happy. Then, the general affairs department arranged for a Chinese lunch, catered by the Star Film Company's kitchen, with twenty tables. The guests devoured the food, and soon the dishes were empty. After the meal, a bell rang in the photography studio, and everyone rushed to the photography studio.

A Glimpse of the Wedding Hall To avoid outside attention, the wedding hall was set up in the Star Film Company's No. 2 photography studio. The hall was designed by the famous set designer Jing Liting, so all the decorations were very magnificent. Around the hall hung scrolls presented by relatives, friends, and local dignitaries, as well as various silver tripods and silver cups, in a dazzling array of colors, making it a grand occasion.

Wedding Ceremony The bell rang three times, and the music started. The wedding of this pair of male and female movie stars began. The bride and groom walked in slowly with smiles. Behind the groom were four groomsmen: You Guangzhao, Wang Jiting, Li Qing, and Sun Min. These four were all acquaintances of the newlyweds. The master of ceremonies was the director with a small mustache, Li Pingqian. The person in charge of maintaining order was the stage manager Bi Hu. When the newlyweds reached the guests, the hundred or so male and female guests threw long strips of colored paper at them. For a time, the hall was filled with the sound of throwing colored paper and cheers. The photographer Wang Shizhen was there to capture the memory of this wedding.

Honeymoon After the Wedding It is said that after their wedding, Gu Lan Jun and Wang Zhengxin will spend their honeymoon in Shanghai, and then explain the wedding process to all the citizens of Shanghai. As for when they will make a public appearance, according to Li Pingqian, it will be around the time of the "Peach and Plum Vie for Glory."

Hu Rongzhi's Foreign Daughter Dance

Lianhua Pictorial Offers Special Rates for Direct Subscribers

Volume 7, Issue 4 is Now Published

Lianhua Pictorial is now seeking 10,000 basic subscribers and offering special rates, domestic half-year (12 issues) for one dollar, full year (24 issues) for one dollar and eighty cents, overseas half-year for two dollars, full year for three dollars and eighty cents, postage included. The deadline is the end of March. The retail price remains ten cents per issue. Those who wish to subscribe can send money to Lianhua Book and Newspaper Agency, 3 Jiao San Street, Xujiahui, Shanghai. Local subscribers can also subscribe directly from the business department of Lianhua Company, 71 Hong Kong Road.

Also, Volume 7, Issue 4 of the publication is now published. The content has been greatly reformed. Starting with Volume 7, Issue 5, the issues will be published punctually. The cover of this issue is Li Zhuozhuo, and the back cover is Li Lili. There are more than twenty illustrations and cartoons. The text includes Bai Jian's "Huang Liushuang Returns Home," a short and sharp piece in "A Few Words," the meaningful "Children Watching Love Scenes," Zhong Shigen's thousand-character film lesson, the first lesson being "Film Stories," an introduction to world film stars in "What I Know About Marlene Dietrich," a record of famous films in "Brief Notes on Sin and Conscience," a report on world news in "World Film Scene Lookout," and a "Film Calendar." The scope of the material has also been greatly expanded. All news from various companies and domestic trends are recorded in detail. Subscribing to Lianhua Pictorial is undoubtedly like having a complete film encyclopedia.
